Reuters Special Commercial Dispatch of the 27th 56

Gold and Silver: London's surplus market was stable this morning, priced at 140 shillings, 10 and a half pence, the same as yesterday.

London's large strips traded sluggishly today. Spot prices were 19 and 9375 pence, futures were 19 and 875 pence, both down by 0625. It is said that speculators sold, but there were not many buyers.

Mountrie large strips future market was weak this morning due to profit-taking by bulls. At the opening, the July price was 15 pounds lower than yesterday's closing price, at 44.60-45.05.

Exchange Rates: In the Anglo-American London foreign exchange market this morning, the price of the pound in US dollars was weaker. The opening exchange rate was 4.955625 US dollars per pound, 1875 lower than the closing rate of the Anglo-American market yesterday. At 11:14, it fell by 5625 to 4.95 US dollars. A few minutes later, it continued to fall by 0625 to 4.949375 US dollars. This price remained unchanged until 1 PM.

Securities

New York: The stock market opened at a flat price, with most securities showing gains. Copper mines, department stores, and automobile stocks rose more significantly. Railroad stocks fell due to speculative pressure. Shortly after the opening, market prices became mixed. Automobile and department store stocks both fell slightly due to profit-taking and bull liquidation. Merchants are taking a wait-and-see attitude due to unrest in Europe. At 11 o'clock, prices of various stocks eased due to continued profit-taking and bull liquidation. Automobile, railroad, and steel stocks fell below yesterday's closing prices. The New York stock market prices are listed on the left:

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton Market: The market opened strong this morning due to purchases by industry and short covering. Within the first half hour, the May contract rose 11 points to 11.22. At 11 o'clock, it continued to rise 11 points due to general buying, reaching 11.33, a net increase of 22 points compared to yesterday's closing price.

Liverpool Cotton Market: Stable today. The May contract rose by two points to six pence due to industry purchases.

Chicago Wheat: Mixed this morning. Prices fluctuated slightly. Opening prices fell due to profit-taking, but later rebounded due to industry purchases and short covering. At 11 o'clock, the May price was 97 cents, 25 higher than yesterday's closing price. Grain futures were firm this morning due to industry purchases. At 11 o'clock, the May price was half a cent higher than yesterday's closing price.

Franco-Belgian-British Military Negotiations. British Foreign Secretary Explains to Germany. Germany Has Abandoned Guaranteed Rights. German Representative Returned Home Yesterday for Instructions. 57

London. British Foreign Secretary Eden held an important meeting with German Ambassador Ribbentrop today, lasting 45 minutes. Ribbentrop asked Eden to explain that in his speech in the House of Commons yesterday, the chiefs of staff of Britain and France are now in consultation regarding the obligations of the Locarno Treaty. It is said that Eden replied that the talks have not yet begun, but seem likely to begin within ten days. Ribbentrop continued to ask for a clearer explanation of the framework under which the talks will proceed. If Britain still considers itself bound by the Locarno Treaty, then Britain also has an obligation to defend Germany's borders from violation, not only the borders of France and Belgium. It is expected that Eden will reply that Britain's obligations as a guarantor only apply to France and Belgium, because Germany has abolished the Locarno Treaty. Both Eden and Ribbentrop believe that Hitler's response to the memorandum of the four countries, Britain, France, Belgium, and Italy, should not be discussed at present. Both believe that the gap between France and Germany can be bridged, so they have decided that negotiations on this issue are best postponed until after the French general election and will begin in mid-May. (27th Reuters Dispatch)

London. German representative Ribbentrop formally raised reservations with Foreign Secretary Eden at noon today regarding the ongoing talks between the British, French, and Belgian general staffs. British officials claimed that Ribbentrop had asked Foreign Secretary Eden about the agreement that could be reached between the British and French general staffs, and the adverse impact this agreement could have on future negotiations. Eden gave a detailed explanation. Ribbentrop completed his mission and boarded a plane at 3 PM today to return to Berlin to report to Head of State Hitler. Once the German government has completed its response to the Locarno Treaty, he will return here. (27th Havas Dispatch)

British Foreign Secretary's Declaration: Adherence to Treaty Obligations; Liaison Between British, French, and Belgian General Staffs: Different from Pre-European War Situation 58

London – Foreign Secretary Eden, at 3:45 PM today, attended the House of Commons and delivered an important speech on the government's foreign policy. The speech lasted for over an hour. The venue was packed, with every seat in the diplomatic corps section filled. The ambassadors from France, Germany, Belgium, and Poland, the U.S. Chief Representative to the Naval Conference, Davis, and ministers from other countries all attended to listen. The grand occasion was rarely seen. Foreign Secretary Eden stated, "The various obligations contained in the Locarno Pact are of great practical significance. As a guarantor of the pact, we are bound by its provisions. Every Foreign Secretary of Britain has adhered to the treaties signed by Britain. Now that I am in charge of foreign affairs, I would rather break my own teeth than violate the treaties. There is no doubt about this." (Havas dispatch of the 26th)

London – British Foreign Secretary Eden, while debating foreign policy in the House of Commons today, delivered a speech requesting the entire House, regardless of party affiliation, to establish a unified national policy and provide common assistance to maintain peace, strengthen the League of Nations, and uphold the dignity of treaties, promising to be consistent and unremitting in their efforts to construct a future that can clear away the existing clouds of sorrow and misery from the current state of troubles and anxieties. Eden's warning was: "We know our responsibilities and are prepared to proceed, but what we consider most important is that we must resolutely seek peace based on a durable foundation. If we want to achieve this goal, we must have the assistance of all sectors of the country."

At the beginning of his speech, Eden stated that his remarks today were not directed at foreign countries but at the British people. He would speak frankly about international events, without concealment, so that the British people could understand the current situation and its difficulties through clear and accurate language. The people must distinguish between national emotions and obligations that are beneficial or detrimental to the nation. The provision in the Treaty of Versailles that the Rhineland should never be garrisoned was the most important factor in France's decision to abandon its demand that the Rhineland be separated from Germany.

Eden then traced the history of the demilitarized zone to ensure France's security and the process by which Germany failed to comply with the procedures stipulated in the freely negotiated treaties. He stated that Germany referred to the Treaty of Versailles as a treaty imposed under duress, in which the Germans had no say. However, no one had ever accused the Locarno Pact of being concluded under duress. If Germany wanted to revise the Locarno Pact, it could engage in negotiations. The issue of whether the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Treaty conflicted with the Locarno Pact should be resolved according to the methods stipulated in the latter. If the Hague Tribunal was deemed inappropriate, the Franco-German arbitration treaty clearly stipulated that legal issues could also be submitted to the Permanent Conciliation Commission. Even those in Britain who believed Germany had sufficient reasons abhorred Germany's actions of using force instead of reason.

Eden then spoke about Britain's position and read out Article 4 of the Locarno Pact, stating that Britain was not an arbiter but a guarantor with real obligations. He wished to explain to the House that he was not prepared to be the first Foreign Secretary to go back on his word. At the same time, according to Article 7 of the Locarno Pact, the British government had an obligation to seek reconciliation and understanding through peaceful means. The current proposal of the four countries aimed at communicating opinions before negotiations. This was not an ultimatum, nor was it an order to be accepted by force. If the international military force was a difficult point and the German government had other alternative suggestions, the British government could prepare to consider them with other countries. However, it was essential to understand that if the German side did not make constructive contributions, the work aimed solely at starting negotiations would be impossible to proceed.

Eden continued, stating that Britain's contribution to the security of France and Belgium had been included in the four-nation proposal, and explained the arrangements for general staff talks. He said that the general staff talks now were very different from those before 1914. In the past, the talks were not accompanied by political understandings, so their significance was not limited. However, the talks now were only limited to the intentions already stated in the political agreement. Some people were now advocating that Britain must avoid various European disputes. It should be known that the security of the territories of France and Belgium must be maintained, and that the troops of other countries must not be allowed to cross their borders. This was a matter of great concern to Britain. The general staff talks only applied to cases of unprovoked aggression. He hoped that actions such as unprovoked aggression, which were conditions for the general staff talks, would never occur. However, he was convinced that once Britain's position was clearly announced, such incidents would not occur.

Regarding the responsibilities that Britain could join as part of the final solution, the guarantees between Western European countries should be reciprocal. Britain would give guarantees to others and would also receive guarantees from others. Security would be shared. All signatories of the Locarno Pact, including Germany, could join this new guarantee.

Eden continued, speaking about the guarantees that Germany and France would receive in the event of a failure to reconcile. He said that apart from the European part involved in the obligations of the Locarno Pact, Britain's guarantee was the same as that of other members of the League of Nations. As for the scope involved in the Locarno Pact, Britain did not have new restrictions but only had ways to more effectively fulfill existing restrictions. He had no regrets about the various proposals contained in the White Paper. The current situation was serious, rarely seen since the war. Few people in Britain understood the great relationship between the demilitarized zone and some parts of Europe. After the publication of the White Paper, any steps that could lead to war were unlikely to take place. Comparing the risk of war with the White Paper, he was convinced that the world would recognize that the White Paper had its own value. The world attached great importance to new negotiations, but new negotiations would only be possible if Germany made a contribution. Germany had not yet made any contribution, only Hitler had committed to not increasing the number of troops in the Rhineland. This was still not enough. If Germany promised not to build defensive works in the Rhineland during the negotiations, it might be helpful. However, from what he had heard, Germany could not even give this commitment.

Eden concluded by saying that the British government had three objectives: eliminating the scourge of war, creating a situation in which new negotiations could be held, and promoting the success of new negotiations, so as to strengthen collective security and facilitate Germany's re-entry into the League of Nations, and to enable larger negotiations on the scope of economic and disarmament, which are essential for European peace, to be held in a more pleasant atmosphere. How will the opportunity to implement the above procedure be? It will depend on Hitler's suggestions next week. He believed that Hitler had understood the efforts made by the British government. He knew that Hitler must know how eagerly Europe expected his proposals. As far as Britain was concerned, we could tell Hitler that we would treat his suggestions with a broad mind and sincere desire, in order to make good use of his suggestions and achieve lasting peace in Europe. There was one more condition for success, namely, a more peaceful atmosphere. The time for crucial international negotiations had just begun. He believed that there were several points that any British Foreign Secretary had to recognize. Britain was not bound by the various policies of France or Germany. What was Britain's policy? It was the League of Nations Covenant and its obligations as a member of the League of Nations. We knew our obligations and were prepared to fulfill them. Eden concluded as follows: "I want to tell France, 'If you are not prepared to deal with the difficult problems that still separate you and Germany with a broad mind, then we will not be able to guarantee peace.' I also want to tell Germany, 'If you are not prepared to make contributions to dispel the European anxiety you have created, how can we hope to participate in any negotiations with success?' The British people, who have peace as their sole purpose, a European solution as their sole desire, and the support of the League of Nations as their sole political proposition, will judge other countries on the spirit and scope of this cooperation." (Reuters dispatch of the 26th)

Speeches by Members of Various Parties in the British House of Commons; Lloyd George Strongly Condemns Military Alliances; The Labour Party Supports Inviting Germany to Return to the League of Nations 59

London – The debate was opened today by Foreign Secretary Eden. Eden spoke at great length, including the statement that he did not want to be the first Foreign Secretary to recognize Britain's treaty obligations. After the Foreign Secretary finished speaking, Dalton spoke on behalf of the Labour Party, criticizing the details of the four-nation proposal, saying that a country that did not support a purely British-French military alliance would support the establishment of a strong organization for collective security formed by the League of Nations. Dalton strongly opposed the suggestion in the Locarno Agreement that the British and French army chiefs of staff jointly plan to defend the French border. George then made a preliminary statement in response. (Reuters dispatch of the 26th)

London – The House of Commons discussed foreign policy yesterday afternoon until 11:00 PM before adjourning. Churchill, the leader of the extreme right wing of the Conservative Party, and Major Attlee, the leader of the Labour opposition, both delivered speeches. The discussion was finally concluded by Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain. (Havas dispatch of the 27th)

London – In the House of Commons' debate on foreign policy today, Sinclair, a Liberal MP, spoke after Labour MP Dalton. He first condemned Germany's actions, but said, "What Germany has done is to remove the shackles of the Treaty of Versailles, which should have been removed long ago." Any treaty that is no longer appropriate should be revised by the League of Nations. Sinclair firmly condemned the plan in the draft Locarno Agreement for British and French troops to be stationed in the German Rhineland. He said that if the troops of the two countries were stationed in the same place, conflicts might occur. He also said that the British government should always faithfully abide by all the obligations contained in the League of Nations Covenant, but should strive to avoid military alliances. Nigel, an MP of the National Labour Party, said, "No one in France, when in power, would agree to a war of aggression, and Germany is a common danger to European countries. All the MPs present here should agree with this statement. Therefore, we should immediately conclude a practical agreement with France so that if France has difficulties before a final solution is reached in the current difficult situation, we can provide full assistance to it. However, it should be stated that this assistance can only be applied in Western Europe." (Havas dispatch of the 26th)

London – After Foreign Secretary Eden finished speaking in the House of Commons this afternoon, Dalton, the former Foreign Secretary, immediately stood up on behalf of the opposition Labour Party and criticized several points of the draft Locarno Agreement. He strongly criticized the provision in the first part of the draft that the 20-kilometer zone inside Germany, east of the Franco-Belgian border, should be assigned to the troops of Britain and Italy to guard, saying, "This suggestion is purely wishful thinking and is extremely absurd. The mutual assistance provisions of the Locarno Pact, as stated in the draft, should be jointly discussed by the general staffs of Britain, France, Italy, and Belgium, are also wishful thinking. As of now, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has been silent and contemptuous, which makes people feel that the British government is now abandoning the League of Nations, unwilling to seek rapprochement within the scope of the League of Nations, and wants to open up a new path to conclude a British-French alliance." Dalton then declared that what we Labour MPs support is not a British-French alliance, but a collective security system, and what we advocate is the Geneva Protocol of 1924. "If Germany refuses to participate in the collective security system, then other countries should also organize a peace system, even if Germany is not in it. Britain should make a clear declaration that Germany should not be allowed to attack Poland, Czechoslovakia, the Soviet Union, or Austria. If British words can be so frank and clear, then there will be no war in Europe." (Havas dispatch of the 26th)

London – Lloyd George, the former Prime Minister and leader of the Liberal Party, spoke in the House of Commons today after Nigel, an MP of the National Labour Party. He said that he was "captivated" by Foreign Secretary Eden's remarks, and that the draft Locarno Agreement, "in my view, is very dangerous, and Eden defended it in every way, with the most skillful rhetoric. I advocate that Germany must obtain equal rights, and I hope that the British government will give Germany a fair opportunity for any suggestions it may put forward, so that it can negotiate calmly." Lloyd George then questioned the government: "Will the mutual assistance measures discussed between the general staffs of the countries concerned be implemented when negotiations break down, or will they be implemented only when an unprovoked act of aggression occurs? This question is related to the lives of millions of young people. The above two levels are vastly different and cannot be confused. I now warn you, MPs, that the military alliance system previously caused the Great War of 1914. If you join the alliance in the future, the result will be a repeat of the past. Countries are now in this dangerous situation. French Foreign Minister Flandin gave a speech in the Chamber of Deputies last week, and all the MPs paid great attention when he mentioned this. Now Foreign Secretary Eden says that the talks between the general staffs of the countries concerned are only the implementation measures of the Locarno Pact, but this is not the case. In my view, these talks are exactly the same as the military alliances that caused the European War in the past."

Sir Chamberlain, the Conservative leader and former Foreign Secretary, then spoke, saying that among the declarations made in Parliament, Foreign Secretary Eden's declaration today was the best. The crux of the problem at this moment was not the long-standing feud between France and Germany, because the treaty obligations destroyed by Germany not only involved France but also affected Belgium. Chamberlain recalled Prime Minister Baldwin's words in March last year, that "Britain's border is not on the coast of Dover, but on the banks of the Rhine," saying that "at this moment, not only France and Belgium are in danger, but also Britain. Because in terms of Britain's security, the freedom and independence of France and Belgium are of great importance, even more so than at any time in the past. What is the most important issue in the future relationship between European countries? That is, Germany is allowed to maintain normal relations with its neighbors, and the country is abiding by the promises it has freely accepted, or whether these promises can only bind other countries, and Germany can discard them at any time, should be determined." Sir Chamberlain finally mentioned the suggestions of Chancellor Hitler, saying that although they were enough to make people feel relieved, "Unfortunately, words and deeds do not match." The 25-year peace plan was also purely wishful thinking, because Germany was also a signatory to the Kellogg-Briand Pact and could not use war as an instrument of national policy. (Havas dispatch of the 26th)

The former Foreign Secretary Chamberlain also declared that the real point of contention today was whether military victory or the rule of law would prevail in the future. If the credibility of treaties could not be restored, it would be impossible to conclude new treaties. Hitler had made various promises, but he had not seen any action to guarantee them. He had proposed a 25-year peace, but Germany was bound by the Kellogg Pact to never use war as an instrument of policy. Germany's statement that it was willing to return to the League of Nations was obviously a request to recover its colonies. Germany's recent anti-Semitism and glorification of war were major issues that should be resolved, not small issues such as the reoccupation of the Rhineland. If we do not learn a lesson, we will quickly see a new 1914.

Churchill then spoke, saying that the real problem was not the reoccupation of the Rhineland, but Germany's rearmament. Countries alarmed by Germany's military expansion should now conclude mutual assistance treaties under the League of Nations Covenant. Any measures that we are unwilling to impose on ourselves should not be imposed on Germany. The security of German territory should be guaranteed. Not only on the Rhineland issue, but also on the major issue of German rearmament, countries should collectively negotiate with Germany, and Germany must be asked to state its grievances. (Reuters dispatch of the 26th)

Attlee, a member of the opposition party, then spoke, praising the Foreign Secretary's handling of difficult negotiations and supporting his policy, saying that the Labour Party agreed to invite Germany to join the League of Nations, but Germany had now lost its credibility. Without its expression to abide by the treaties from now on, inviting it to join would be purely wishful thinking. Countries should now advocate that Germany should contribute to peace and security.

Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain concluded the debate for the government, saying that we must now go through a long process before we can rely on the members of the League of Nations to cooperate in punishing aggressors. At the same time, we must think that the Locarno Agreement has strengthened the League of Nations. The Chancellor then mentioned George's question, that the treaty signed by the British and French chiefs of staff obliged Britain to cooperate with France in driving the German troops out of the Rhineland, saying, "There is no such thing." He then said that Germany had not yet contributed to restoring its credibility. What we want is for Germany to prove to other countries that it has a genuine desire to participate in the meeting to obtain a satisfactory solution. After the Chancellor finished speaking, the meeting was adjourned without a vote. (Reuters dispatch of the 26th)

Pacific Fortifications: The U.S. Is Unwilling to Negotiate After Japan Abrogates Treaty 60

London – It was announced here today that after Japan withdraws from the London Naval Treaty, the United States is temporarily unwilling to discuss the issue of fortifications in the Pacific. Britain had inquired with the United States for its opinion. The U.S. delegation replied that after Japan's withdrawal from the meeting, this issue could no longer be on the agenda. However, it is generally believed that if Japan can sign a new treaty in the future, the United States may still discuss the issue of fortifications. (National Telegram of the 26th)

London – Naval experts attending the meeting here today said that the goodwill and economic strength between naval powers can prevent wasteful naval competition. The newly established tripartite treaty between Britain, France, and the United States should eliminate international suspicion and reduce the risk of the sudden appearance of new types of warships. As for other effects, it all depends on the rationality of the international community. The Japanese representative stated today that although representatives of several countries spoke when signing the treaty, requesting Japan to abide by the terms of the new treaty, it is doubtful whether Japan is willing to abide by it. If Japan cannot agree to reduce the limit on the caliber of guns from 16 inches to 14 inches before New Year's Day next year, then the provision will be automatically canceled. (National Telegram of the 26th)

Washington – Well-informed sources here said today that the world's naval powers all know that naval competition is inevitable, but only a calm mind and agile diplomacy can avoid it. Because the newly established naval treaty between Britain, France, and the United States does not limit the number of warships, whether there will be competition in the future depends entirely on Japan's policy and the situation in Europe. If Japan is willing to limit its fleet and still maintain a ratio that is not much different from the current one, then dangerous competition may be avoided. Although Japan has stated that it should have equal rights with the British and American navies, it has not yet announced its intention to implement this right. Therefore, most of the international naval construction competition must depend on Japan's policy on this point. However, the policies of Germany and Italy also have a direct impact on the British and French navies. Italy may expand its fleet because British ships are stationed in the Mediterranean. As a result, naval competition will also arise. Currently, the United States has the largest fleet in the world, with a total of 342 warships, Britain has 303, Japan has 212, France has 209, Italy has 182, and Germany has 42. However, the U.S. fleet is very old. If only warships that meet the age requirements are considered, there are only 87, Britain has 146, Japan has 149, France has 144, Italy has 119, and Germany has 32. The United States has now determined a plan for expansion and replacement in order to remedy the situation. There are already 84 ships under construction that have been designated, and they will be built soon. At the same time, Britain also has 49 ships under construction, and Japan has 35. The U.S. construction program includes 3 aircraft carriers, 3 heavy cruisers, 9 light cruisers, 52 destroyers, and 16 submarines. A naval expert predicted that the United States would soon expand its naval bases among its territories in the Pacific in order to resist the impact of the treaty's restrictions on the construction of heavy cruisers. If naval ports are established on Samoa Island, Guam, and Alaska, and the facilities in Hawaii and the Philippines are expanded, then the value of all 20 heavy cruisers of the United States will be twice as much as it is now. Senior U.S. naval authorities also deeply feel the need for this in order to cope with the larger cruiser strength of Britain and Japan. Because Japan is compact and Britain has a dense network of military ports and many merchant ships, they are the wings of the navy. (National Telegram of the 26th)

Tokyo – On the morning of the 26th, Fujii, the acting ambassador to Britain, visited Councillor Craigie of the British Foreign Office and expressed the Japanese government's views on the submarine usage restriction proposal as follows:

The Japanese government has no objection in principle to retaining Article 4 regarding submarine usage restrictions in the London Treaty.

However, the form of its retention should avoid establishing a new treaty or a similar form.

In the new treaty established this time, the provision on the use of submarines exists independently in the form of a protocol. This form does not meet the wishes of the Japanese government. Please reconsider and change its form. After 45 minutes, Acting Ambassador Fujii resigned. It is heard that the British government will reconsider the issue of the above form. (Domei News Agency dispatch of the 26th)

Tokyo – The Naval System Investigation Committee has been holding policy, organization reform, and budget sub-committee meetings for days to investigate data and review reform methods. As a result, the reform of the naval system is a necessary thing to implement. The various organizations within the current navy department have been greatly reduced in personnel and organizational expenses due to the influence of the Washington and London treaties, and most of the budget has been transferred to increasing warships and aviation troops, resulting in a one-sided phenomenon. However, when the naval treaty is eliminated at the beginning of 1937, it will be difficult to bear the major tasks of fulfilling national defense and strengthening combat effectiveness with the current content. Therefore, it is necessary to reorganize the organization of the Zhenshoufu Yaogangbu (various important locations for naval defense) within the department in order to achieve the purpose. (Domei News Agency dispatch of the 27th)

After a Conflict Near Changlingzi, Japanese and Russian Troops Both Retreat; Detailed Report on the Border Conflict in Outer Mongolia 61

Tokyo – Regarding the Changlingzi incident, as of the 27th,

According to information received by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, it is known that Japanese and Soviet

troops have both withdrawn approximately five li, centered on their respective national borders,

and have gathered there to ease the confrontation,

temporarily calming the situation. Therefore, this incident is unlikely to escalate. As for the Soviet Union, since the February 26th Incident,

the fact that considerable troops have been moved to the Soviet-Manchurian border area

is true, and the Japanese side is paying close attention to this. (27th, Domei News Agency)

Tokyo – Ambassador Ueta, stationed in Manchuria, reported the following to the First Bureau of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs regarding the Changlingzi incident: On the 25th, at 8:10 AM,

Lieutenant Kajiwara of the unit stationed in Yanji, along with four men, and Sergeant Ogura of the Hunshun Detachment with five men,

went to inspect the border area of Changlingzi, Hunshun County. They were suddenly

ambushed by eight members of the Changlingzi GPU. There was no warning beforehand. As a result, Lieutenant Kajiwara,

Second Lieutenant Fukushima, and Sergeant Ogura of the Hunshun Detachment all suffered injuries of varying degrees. As for First Class Medical Officer Minoda and Private First Class Yoshida,

their whereabouts are unknown. This incident, without any prior warning,

constitutes an illegal attack on Japanese officers and soldiers undergoing training on the Manchurian-Soviet border. The responsibility

lies with the Soviet side. The judgment of right and wrong is extremely clear.

The responsibility for this illegal act should be borne entirely by the Soviet GPU,

and so on. (27th, Domei News Agency)

Dalian – General Kenkichi Ueda, Commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army, passed through Andong Station at 11:00 AM this morning en route to Manchuria. According to him,

the conflict between the Japanese and Soviet troops at Changlingzi is a local issue

and will not escalate. The established policy of resolving border disputes

will not be adversely affected in any way. (27th, China United Press)

Moscow – According to a report from Kulun, at 3:15 PM on March 24th,

a unit of Japanese-Manchukuo troops in three large trucks

attacked a Mongolian border guard outpost in the area of Lake Buurnuur in Mongolia. The attackers were reinforced by four more trucks

and immediately opened fire. The Mongolian outpost fought bravely and resisted,

forcing the invading troops to retreat back into Manchurian territory. The Mongolian border guards suffered no losses in this engagement. On the morning of March 25th,

two hundred Japanese-Manchukuo troops concentrated in the fishing village area two kilometers from the lake.

In the evening, they fired rifles and machine guns at the Mongolian outpost,

and simultaneously fired two cannons. The Mongolian border guards returned fire,

but due to the disparity in numbers between them and the Japanese-Manchukuo troops, they retreated under cover of darkness from that location

to the shallow waters of the lake seven kilometers from the Outer Mongolian border. On the dawn of March 26th, the Japanese-Manchukuo troops, seeing that the Mongolian outpost

had withdrawn, crossed the Khalkhyn Gol River and occupied the outpost

until 1:00 PM. They spotted a Mongolian plane in the conflict area

and began to retreat. Subsequently, the Japanese-Manchukuo troops crossed the river and returned to Manchurian territory. However, because the Japanese-Manchukuo troops were still concentrated in the area,

their attack on the Mongolian border guards could erupt at any time.

(27th, TASS)

The Complexity of Japanese Politics: Observations from the Editor of an English Newspaper in Tokyo 62

Los Angeles – Mr. Freitsch, the owner of the well-known English-language newspaper "Japan Advertiser"

published in Japan, has arrived in Los Angeles and stated that the Japanese military will control the government even more powerfully in the future.

The problems involved in the current Japanese political situation

are so complex that they cannot be understood by the United States. Only when a military faction advocating

leniency gains power will Japan's difficulties be effectively resolved. The recent disturbances in Japan are merely

a scene in a deeply rooted movement. This movement, since the September 18th Manchurian Incident,

has been ongoing and intensifying.

Although the army authorities have tried their best to conceal

the fact that there are differences of opinion within the army, the existence of rebels

has been undeniable for several years. The September 18th Incident

was, in fact, a mutiny by the Japanese army in Manchuria. Shigeru Honjo, who was then the commander of the Japanese army in Manchuria, could

be suspected for his inability to restrain his subordinates. At the time, the Army Minister and the Cabinet could have recalled Honjo,

but considering future events, the nation had to endorse

it. After the assassination of Tsuyoshi Inukai on May 15, 1932,

General Araki, a powerful figure in the nationalist faction, was appointed

as Army Minister. It was expected that he could restrain the dissatisfied

elements within the army. Although the mutinies in the Japanese army were limited to dissatisfied

young officers, this rebellion was actually encouraged by those within and outside the army.

Japanese law prohibits communism and often searches for

communists, but there are indeed numerous

groups that go beyond the scope of patriotism. Their primary platform

is to support the Emperor, while

other platforms have an anti-capitalist and socialist nature. These

young officers and patriotic group leaders do not want what

Europeans call a fascist system, but rather want a military

socialist regime. The Emperor's advisors are doing their

utmost to quell this radical movement, and as a result, the young officers

are assassinating politicians around the Emperor who advocate leniency.

Current and recent events may have caused a reaction,

making the masses aware of the lurking dangers. However, this

movement has spread widely, and even those in close contact with the Japanese government,

such as the Prime Minister himself, find it difficult to determine the impact of this reaction.

According to Mr. Freitsch, who has been in the United States for two months recuperating,

he is now preparing to return to Tokyo. (27th, Reuters)

Venizelos' Remains Returned to His Native Country; Greek Government Orders a Day of Mourning 64

Athens – Eleftherios Venizelos, a famous Greek politician

who served as Prime Minister eight times, passed away last week

in Paris at the age of seventy-two. His remains are being transported by destroyer to

Crete for burial. Yesterday, as the ship passed through the Corinth

Canal, the banks were crowded with onlookers. Many women wept

and threw flowers into the sea to express their respect. The government has ordered

today to be a national day of mourning, and all activities have been suspended

to commemorate his passing. Although Venizelos launched an uprising against

the government last year, failing and fleeing to France, his past

contributions to national affairs are not forgotten. (27th, Reuters)

Lalgani Port, Crete, Greece – Eleftherios Venizelos, the former Prime Minister

and leader of the Liberal Party, who passed away in Paris on the 18th of this month,

had his coffin returned to the country. A grand

funeral was held here this morning at 10:00 AM. Crown Prince Paul, the Speaker of the Parliament,

and Sophoulis, the current leader of the Liberal Party, personally

held the ropes of the hearse, all with faces of grief. The coffin was placed on a gun carriage.

The Crown Prince, Venizelos' family, government ministers,

local authorities, etc., followed behind the hearse. The entire city,

including the artillery batteries, was in mourning. Venizelos' coffin will

lie in state at the Church of the Virgin Mary for several days to allow the public to pay their

respects. He will then be buried opposite Venizelos' former residence,

in a tomb built by the city authorities. (27th, Havas)

Death of Japanese Minister of Commerce and Industry Kawasaki 65

Tokyo – Since the 12th of this month,

Minister of Commerce and Industry Kawasaki has been resting at home due to

a cold. However, on the morning of the 27th, his condition suddenly deteriorated, becoming life-threatening.

Financial Turmoil in France and Germany: Mark Expected to Devalue, French Francs Sold Off; President of Deutsche Bank to Resign 67

Paris – French francs were sold off again in Europe today.

The British Equalisation Fund had to provide large-scale

support. The French public is gradually becoming aware that the current situation cannot be remedied by orthodox financial methods.

The flight of French capital has caused the selling price to rise sharply,

rising faster than the retail price, making it increasingly difficult to sell French francs.

The latest weekly report released by French banks

shows an increase of 6,050,000,000 francs in banknote circulation,

and an increase of 1,000,000,000 francs in discounted bills. Gold reserves decreased by 0.

56. (27th, Reuters)

London – The Daily Mail recently reported that financial circles in London and Berlin

believe that the German Minister of Economics and President of the Deutsche Bank, Hjalmar Schacht,

will undoubtedly submit his resignation after the general election to the Reichstag on the 29th of this month.

This is because the left wing of the German National Socialist Party is now advocating devaluing the mark

and is putting pressure on Schacht. Schacht is unwilling to yield and would rather resign. (27th,

Havas)

Berlin – The rumor that Hjalmar Schacht, the President of the German Reichsbank, is about to resign

has intensified today after the publication of the bank's annual report.

Traditionally, the bank's report would state that the stability of the mark must be maintained at all costs,

but this resolution only states that the bank's duty is to provide an orderly monetary situation.

The market believes that the change in wording in the bank's report indicates the possibility of a change in German monetary policy.

As everyone knows, the extremist National Socialists have recently been putting pressure on

Schacht to obtain a more flexible monetary situation. Schacht's position as President of the Reichsbank

conflicts with his concurrent position as Minister of Economics. After Schacht became Minister, he wanted to promote

Germany's foreign trade. It is expected that Schacht will resign from his position at the bank

and remain as Minister of Economics for a long term. (27th, Reuters)

Hunan-Guizhou-Yunnan Highway 70

—From Initial Construction to Improvement—

Guiyang Correspondence: Our country is vast in territory, and although there has been considerable progress in road construction in recent years thanks to the efforts of people in and out of government, according to a recent survey, the country has only more than 84,000 kilometers of highways. This is far from the one million miles (equivalent to 1.6 million kilometers) of crushed stone roads that Premier Sun Yat-sen envisioned in his "The International Development of China". It can be said that the southwestern provinces are located on the periphery, and transportation is obstructed. Not only have the natural resources not been developed, resulting in poverty, but also the Zhu-Mao communist bandits used the area as a refuge two years ago. Fortunately, the Central Army tracked them down and gradually eliminated them. At that time, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek realized the importance of developing transportation in the southwest, which was urgent. Therefore, he immediately telegraphed the Highway Department of the Military Council, ordering it to first rush the construction of the Hunan-Guizhou Highway, with the aim of gradually promoting it. Now that the Hunan-Guizhou Road has been completed, he ordered the continued construction of the Guizhou-Yunnan Highway, and the reorganization of the Guiyang-North section of the Sichuan-Guizhou Road, and the Guiyang-East section of the Hunan-Guizhou Road. Therefore, the engineering situation and construction plans of each road are briefly described below.

Route Survey

The Hunan Highway Bureau originally planned two routes, the Hunan-Guizhou route and the Hunan-Sichuan route. The Hunan-Guizhou route goes from Xiangtan, via Binqing, to Hongjiang, and then to Zhihuang. The Hunan-Sichuan route goes from Taoyuan, via Yuanling, around Baojing, and to Liye Si. The former is biased towards the southeast, and the latter is towards the northwest. Moreover, the routes pass through overlapping mountains, making construction even more difficult. Later, the Highway Department of the Military Council dispatched Chief Engineer Li Yu to personally survey the routes, and examine the agricultural, mining, industrial, and commercial conditions. After detailed research, he selected a more suitable route between the two, which is the current route from Changde, via Taoyuan, Yuanling, Chenxi, Zhijiang, directly to Huangxian. However, there are still two ferry crossings between Changde and Taoyuan, which are very inconvenient for travelers. Therefore, a new route was re-established along the east bank of the Yuan River to avoid them. Therefore, the route surveyed this time has many advantages compared to the original route.

Planning Process

After the route of the road was determined, the Highway Department of the Military Council immediately moved to Yuanling, and based on the determined route, conducted separate surveys and estimated the project budget, which required 2.1 million yuan. In addition to the 300,000 yuan approved by the Military Council, the remaining funds were borrowed by the Hunan Provincial Government from the Shanghai banking group for 1.8 million yuan using 3 million yuan of construction bonds. Once the funds were determined, the Hunan-Guizhou Highway Engineering Office was organized, and Yu Jichuan, the Director of the Hunan Construction Department, was appointed as the head. On the one hand, technical personnel were borrowed from Hunan and Zhejiang provinces to actively carry out the work. The entire line was divided into eight sections to start construction. From Dangde to Taoyuan was called the Detong Section, Taoyuan to Yuanling was called the Taoyuan Section, and the six sections above Yuanling were recorded in order by numbers. However, western Hunan is poor and the procurement and transportation of all materials and workers' food rice were extremely difficult. Therefore, an office was established in Changsha, and transfer stations were added along the line to provide supplies.

Engineering Progress

The Hunan-Guizhou Highway starts from Deshan in Changde and ends at Yuyu shop in Yuping, with a total length of 458 kilometers. Except for stone bridge and culvert contracts, the earthwork project was generally done by migrant workers who were given subsidies. Along the route, the county chiefs served as supervisors, responsible for managing the conscription of labor. At the same time, more than 10,000 people were mobilized, spread across the entire line, and carried out in order. Construction began at the end of April last year, and the entire project was completed at the end of August of the same year.

Guizhou-Yunnan Highway

Overview of Past and Present

From Guiyang via Qingzhen, Pingba to Anshun, the journey is about 90 kilometers. The roadbed and pavement have been built and opened to traffic. From Anshun to Huangguoshu, it is about 55 kilometers. The roadbed has been completed, but most of the pavement is damaged. A section near Huangguoshu has a very steep slope, which cannot be traveled without major repairs. From Huangguoshu via Yongning Annan to Panxian, the total length is 250 kilometers. Although there are places that have been repaired, according to the engineer's survey report, more than 65% cannot be used and new routes must be opened. The usable parts must also be reorganized. Therefore, the Highway Department of the Military Council appointed Chen Zhanxi, Director of the Guizhou Provincial Construction Department, as the director of the Guizhou-Yunnan Road, and established two general section engineering offices. Engineers Xu Mingjie and Zou Yuesheng were appointed to be in charge of engineering affairs, surveying and building as they went, in order to speed up the process. The earthwork project was handled by conscripting labor from the line and nearby counties according to the Hunan-Guizhou Highway method, and subsidies were given. The mountain opening project has been carried out by transferred northern engineering corps. Bridge and culvert projects are contracted separately. It is estimated that the road can be completed and opened to traffic in March or April this year. Above Luodian County, the Yunnan Provincial Government is responsible for construction, and it is also expected to be completed at the same time.

Engineering and Funding

The Yunnan-Guizhou Road is an important part of the Beijing-Yunnan National Highway, and the construction cannot be delayed. However, the route spans the Miaoling Mountains, with towering mountains, steep cliffs, and dangerous rocks. The difficulty of the project is incomparable to other roads. The road began surveying in October last year and started construction in sections in late November. Now, except for the 30 kilometers west of the Panjiang River, which has not yet been surveyed, the rest have been surveyed and construction has begun. As for the construction cost, if it is designed according to strict highway standards, it would cost 10,000 yuan per kilometer. Now, due to the short time and financial difficulties, the estimated total project cost is 910,000 yuan. However, Guizhou Province's financial resources are stretched, and most of the construction costs must be requested from the central government. The central government is also facing financial difficulties and has only approved a subsidy of 400,000 yuan. Therefore, the road project can only be planned and constructed within the scope of funds. The current Highway Department of the Military Council and the Guizhou Provincial Government are planning to find ways to increase funding, so that it can be completed on schedule.

Reorganization of the East Road

The Guibei Road, that is, the Guizhou section of the Hunan-Guizhou Highway, except for the section from Guiyang to Pingyue Ganba Shao, which was completed and opened to traffic earlier, now only connects the Yu village of Pingyue Ganba Shao to Wang village, which is 475 li long, of which there are 250 kilometers. It was originally established by the 2nd Route Army Headquarters of the Suppression Bandit Army, the Hunan-Guizhou Road Guizhou East Section Engineering Office and the Supervision Office, responsible for construction, dividing it into four engineering offices and thirty-eight sections, using military labor, ordinary labor, and hourly labor for construction. The original budget was 660,000 yuan, which was directly approved and applied by the Military Council. Construction started in March last year and was completed on August 31st. However, due to the urgency of time and insufficient funding, the selection of routes, the arrangement of slopes and bends, and the equipment of bridges and culverts were not perfect. Therefore, although the roadbed was completed, driving was dangerous. Later, the Highway Department of the Military Council sent personnel to survey and found that the steepness of the roads such as Goose Wing in Shibing Section, Wende Pass and Zhenxiong Pass in Zhenyuan Section, Panshan Xiangshui in Sansui Section, and Xianren Bridge in Qingxi Section were always above 15% to 25%. The bends of the roads in the mountains (commonly known as electric light lines) are mostly below 5 meters to 2 meters in radius. They have actually become a single-corner line. The roads on acute-angled bends have steep slopes, and the slopes of bends with a radius of less than 5 meters are also above 10%. The steep slopes of the adjacent bends are all dangerous and need to be improved. There are also many places where bridges, culverts, and drainage ditches need to be repaired. Therefore, the Reorganization Guizhou East Road Engineering Office was organized, and northern stonemasons were sent to start reorganizing the most dangerous Wende Pass, Zhenxiong Pass, Goose Wing, and Wangcheng Slope. The estimated budget is 130,000 yuan. It has now been completed and opened to traffic. It is continuing to survey the roads that should be changed west of Shibing and gradually improved.

Reorganization of Gui North Road

The Gui North Road, that is, the Guizhou section of the Sichuan-Guizhou Highway. Former Chairman of Guizhou Province, Zhou Xicheng, established the Road Administration Bureau for military relations and built the Gui Chima Road. The route goes from Guiyang via Xifeng, Zunyi, Tongzi, Guanshui, to Chishui. After the road was built to Tongzi, it was suspended due to the political changes in Guizhou Province. When Mao Guangxiang was in charge of Guizhou, he wanted to connect the transportation between Sichuan and Guizhou provinces. Therefore, he sent the former Director of Construction Department, Bin Juren, to survey the route with Sichuan Province, with Chongxi River as the intersection. Liu Jiefeng, the Deputy Director of the Highway Bureau, was appointed to supervise the construction of the Tongchong section, with salt tax surcharge as funding. In the spring of last year, Chairman Chiang Kai-shek urgently wanted to complete the Sichuan-Guizhou Road and still appointed Liu to be responsible for the Tongchong section. The General Staff also appointed Staff Officer Chen Keming to supervise the construction. The estimated budget was approved by Chen's staff and totaled more than 100,000 yuan. Later, Liu was imprisoned for some reason and was presided over by Staff Officer Chen. The Wujiang section was built by the arsenal of the Pacification Commissioner's Office stationed in Guizhou. By June last year, the Tongchong section of the earthen road was completed. At the same time, the Sichuan section was also completed. Therefore, it was possible to travel directly from Guiyang to Chongqing.

Reorganization Status

This route is 360 kilometers long from Guiyang to Xixi River. Because the terrain is dangerous, the mountains overlap, and the construction process is complicated, the engineering is mostly not up to standard, and driving is often dangerous. Later, the Highway Department of the Military Council sent engineer Wu Guoyun to survey the route. The following is an excerpt from his report on the current situation: Gui Tong Section: This section was not surveyed in detail and was mostly based on the original terrain. Therefore, there are many bends even on flat ground, and the slope fluctuates. Moreover, the roadbed is too badly damaged, uneven, and the mountain road is too narrow. It takes two times to back up the car before it can move forward. Moreover, steep bends often have steep slopes. Passengers are always worried when passing through here. There are also too few bridges, culverts, and ditches, which are not enough to drain the water. Most of those that exist are also decayed. Tongchong Section: This section is the most difficult part of the entire line. Although it is only more than 160 li, the mountains are steep and the roads are rugged. All difficult places have not been completed. There are several places where the slope is as high as 25%, and there are many places where it is 17% or 18%. Moreover, there are many sharp bends in the large slope, and there are uphill roads in the downhill routes, which further increases the slope. Therefore, the basic repair must be changed. The retaining walls that are built where the mountains are steep and there is no way to fill the soil are not built legally. As a result, they collapse after heavy rain. The incomplete drainage equipment is even worse than the Guitong section. A small number of road surfaces are paved. The most important bridge is the Sanyi River Bridge, which is 20 meters long. It was completely washed away by the flood shortly after completion. Seeing this, you can know its dangerous situation. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek believed that this road must be improved urgently and strictly ordered the Highway Department of the Military Council and the Guizhou Provincial Government to be responsible for the reconstruction. Therefore, in October last year, the Gui North Road Engineering Office was organized. Wei Yuanzhou, the construction director of Guizhou, served as the director, and engineer Wu Wenyun served as the deputy. First, the route on the north bank of the Wujiang River between Guiyang and Tongzi, and the wharf, bridges, culverts, and other projects were modified. A surveying team was first organized to carry out surveying and construction section by section. As for the reorganization project of the Gui Tong section, after the start of construction, Director Chen was stationed in Tong to supervise. In the past few months, the road project has been 80% or 90% completed and will be completed soon.

It is known that transportation in the southwest has always been inconvenient. Guizhou and Yunnan provinces are known as mountain countries, and transportation is even more difficult. Transportation construction is nothing more than railways, aviation, and highways. Although air transportation has been opened on the Beijing-Yunnan route last year, it is limited by load and is not suitable for the needs of ordinary society. In addition, the climate between Guizhou and Yunnan is bad, with rain and fog, and the route is often blocked and dangerous. Highways can only facilitate military affairs and the transportation of light industrial products. As for the fundamental plan, it still depends on the railway. Recently, the Southwest Railway has been actively prepared by the authorities. I hope that the people of the country will work hard to assist and promote its realization.

Soaring Rice Prices in Xiamen 71

The Municipal Government Forms an Evaluation Committee for Relief

Rice Merchants Request a Reduction in Taxes on Imported Rice

Xiamen Correspondence: Rice prices in Xiamen have risen from 12 yuan to 15 yuan per 100 kilograms in recent weeks, which has greatly affected the people's food, especially the poor. Stores with a slightly larger population will suddenly increase their daily rice expenditure by about one yuan. Zhangzhou and Quanzhou also experienced the same rice price panic. In order to stabilize rice prices, the municipal government specially appointed Wang Zhenmin, the chief of the first section, to convene the Chamber of Commerce and the Rice Industry Association to form a food evaluation committee to discuss methods for stabilizing rice prices and providing relief. Although rice prices have fallen slightly on the 24th and 25th, they have not yet returned to their original state. Rice merchants then submitted a request to the Chamber of Commerce to forward to the municipal government, requesting a reduction in rice tax on imported rice and an exemption from rice donation for exported Zhangzhou rice. It is known that the Fujian Province is not a rice-producing area. Only Zhangzhou in southern Fujian produces rice, but it is not enough to supply the needs of Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, and Xiamen. In the past, rice for Quanzhou and Xiamen was mostly supplied by Annam, Siam, and Rangoon. Since 1933, in order to provide relief to rural areas, import taxes on imported rice were collected. After Xiamen reduced the tax by half, the import of imported rice decreased significantly. Later, the full tax was levied, and the import of imported rice disappeared. The people's food in Quanzhou and Xiamen, in addition to relying on Zhangzhou rice, also relies on the so-called "Shanghai rice" from the Yangtze River. In the past, Zhangzhou rice and Bailan rice cost more than 6 yuan per stone (100 catties), and imported rice cost more than 5 yuan. Since the full tax on imported rice eliminated imports, the provincial government resumed the collection of Zhangzhou rice export donations of one yuan per package (160 catties) last winter. Zhang rice, which is every stone, immediately rose to seven yuan. In recent weeks, it has suddenly risen to eight yuan and six jiao. Xiamen needs 700 bags of rice every day, but according to a survey on the 24th, there are still more than 20,000 bags of rice in Xiamen, and there is also a lot of rice in Zhangzhou. It is not a rice shortage, but the rice price is still high. According to rice merchants, "the reason is that landlords and wealthy farmers in Zhangzhou hoard and speculate, and financial merchants also speculate in hoarding rice and refuse to sell it. For many years, southern Fujian has regarded imported rice as a regulator. The full tax on Tianjin rice is 2 yuan and 5 jiao per 100 catties, and 4 yuan and 3 jiao per package. Imported rice must be sold at about 9 yuan per 100 catties in Xiamen to make a profit. Since imported rice cannot be imported, the only thing that can be used to regulate it is "Shanghai rice". If the price of rice in Shanghai is high, the prices in Quanzhou and Xiamen will also be high. In Guangdong, the import of foreign rice is 1 yuan, 7 jiao, 2 fen, and 8 li per 100 yuan, which is equivalent to 1 yuan and 4 jiao in national currency, which is 1 yuan and 1 jiao less than Xiamen. Therefore, in order to stabilize the rice prices in Xiamen, Zhangzhou, and Quanzhou, it is appropriate to restore the half tax on imported rice. With imported rice regulation, rice prices will not be easily raised" (March 26).

Jiangxi and Anhui Provinces Jointly Discuss Loans for Tea Farmers 72

And Form a Sales Committee

Nanchang Correspondence: Our country's exports mainly include silk, tea, and tung oil. Jiangxi used to sell Ninghong (that is, Xiushui black tea) to Europe, America, and Nanyang countries. In 1928, 117,578 dan of black tea from Ninghong Qimen and other places were imported into our country, worth 2,452,874 taels of silver. In recent years, it has gradually declined. According to Jiujiang Customs statistics, Jiangxi tea exports were about 270,000 to 220,000 dan (100 catties) per year in the Qing Dynasty, and only 10,000 dan in 1932. In the past two years, tea trees in Xiushui area have been cut down as firewood, the leaves are old and no one picks them, and most of the tea gardens have been leveled into wasteland. Now that Qingming is approaching, it is the peak time for tea production. In the past, at this time of year, villagers gathered in Xiushui, Qimen, Wuhu, Deyu, Fuliang, and other counties, and thousands of tea workers picked tea. The songs of tea picking could be heard far and wide. Recently, the villagers are hesitant to move, and the money houses that lend money also have no money to lend. Tea farmers are sitting and waiting to die, tea workers have no livelihood, let alone improving and regaining international sales channels. The authorities of Anhui Province believe that the four counties of Wuyuan, Deyu, and Fuliang, which border Jiangxi and Anhui, are intertwined, especially in terms of economy and the entire foreign affairs, which cannot be separated. Therefore, they specially sent He Jiepu and Lu Zhenmu to Jiangxi to discuss methods to rescue the tea industry. Province Chairman Xiong Shihui believed that this move was related to the national economy and the people's livelihood and was extremely important. He convened the Provincial Committee Xiao Chun Jin, and Li, Acting Director of the Construction Department, the Special Commissioner of the First District, the National Economic Commission, Transportation, Yumin, and representatives of the two banks to jointly discuss the methods with He and Lu. A decision was made that the Bank of Communications would lend 800,000 yuan, and the local banks of Jiangxi and Anhui provinces would jointly lend 500,000 yuan, totaling 1.3 million yuan, to tea farmers. The National Economic Commission and the governments of Anhui and Jiangxi provinces would organize a sales cooperation committee to establish transportation offices in Jiujiang and Shanghai to seek outward sales. After the discussion, He and Lu have returned to Anhui to report, so as to proceed separately. In addition, regarding Ninghong, in addition to the establishment of a normal tea garden and manufacturing plant by the Jiangxi Provincial Agricultural College and the Construction Department, Yumin Bank, the Construction Department, and the Rural Service Area of the Economic Commission will also provide loans to handle all matters related to transportation and sales, in order to reverse the decline of the tea industry.

Recent Conditions of Mineral Resources in Anhui Province 73

——Last Year's Coal Production Reached 700,000 Tons——

Wuhu Communication: Anhui Province is extremely rich in mineral resources, such as Huaining.

Dongliu, Susong, Wangjiang, Suxian, Tongling, Qingyang, Guichi,

Wuhu, Fanchang, Chaoxian, Hanshan, and other counties' anthracite coal; Guangde,

Jingxian, Xuancheng, Ningguo, Huaiyuan, and other counties' bituminous coal;

Dangtu, Fanchang, Tongling, and other counties' iron; Jixi's antimony;

Guichi's alunite; Lujiang's alum; Qianshan, Taihu, Huo

Shan, Luan, Lihuang, and other counties' placer iron, are all being mined by the government and businesses,

yielding substantial profits. Other minerals, such as Xiuning County's [missing character], Chuxian's

copper, Jixi County's gold, Qingyang County's gypsum, have also been

discovered and are planned for mining. As for metal ores yet to be discovered,

it is said there are still many. The scientific verification of mineral composition is undertaken

by the Science Museum jointly established by the Construction and Education Departments, and this spring, a geological

mineral resources survey team will be established to investigate mineral resource distribution, in order

to facilitate development. All operating mines in the province can be divided into three types: state-owned, provincial, and privately operated. The provincially operated mines include two coal mines: Mantoushan and Shuidong. The Mantoushan Coal Mine

was leased to Xie Ji Company in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), and its performance has been good. The Shuidong Coal Mine

was leased to miner Yao Yugeng in the 22nd year of the Republic (1933). Due to handling

the transfer of mining rights, the start of operations was delayed. In addition, more than ten coal mine

areas have been reserved, but their rights have not yet been surveyed and licensed. The state-owned mines

include the Huainan and Lieshan coal mines. The Huainan Coal Mine is operated

by the Construction Committee, with a daily coal production of over 1,000 tons. The Lieshan Coal Mine was originally operated by miner Ni Daolang, and in the 16th year of the Republic (1927), it was taken over by the National Army for the Ministry of Industry to operate. It has now been changed to

a joint public-private operation. As for privately operated mines, most are coal mines, followed by iron mines. Alum and antimony mines are next. The number of newly licensed mining areas

is also increasing daily. As of now, there are a total of 85 licensed private mines, including 70 coal mines, one iron ore and sulfur mine

, and one sulfur mine, covering an area of 3,393 hectares, 49 ares, and 9 square millimeters.

Newly applied for mining areas by businesses include a total of 44 areas, including 38 coal mines, one gold mine,

one antimony mine, and four alunite mines, covering an area of 1,507 hectares, 26 ares, and 12 square millimeters. As for the total amount of mineral production, last year, a total of 400,715 tons of iron sand were produced, and the estimated coal production was around 700,000 tons.

4,000 tons of alum were produced, and the production of sulfur and antimony was several

hundred tons each. The total output of the above minerals is more than one million tons,

which is more than in previous years. A gold mine discovered in Jixi County

is also being planned for mining by the government and businesses through separate channels. (26th)

Suzhou

Stalemate in Business Tax Dispute

The Wuxian various trade guilds are opposing

the Business Tax Bureau's direct collection of business tax. It is learned that the Jiangsu

Provincial Department of Finance has specially dispatched Yu Peng to Suzhou to meet with the county government, the Business Tax Bureau, and the

chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, inviting representatives from various industries to a meeting at the county government the day before yesterday.

However, only a dozen or so representatives from various industries attended, and representatives from important industries

were absent. At that time, Yu Peng expressed the Department of Finance's opinion that business tax must be collected directly. However, due to the absence of most industry representatives,

there was no concrete resolution, and the meeting adjourned. Yesterday (the 27th), representatives from various chambers of commerce inquired about everything, so Chairman Cheng of the Chamber of Commerce,

believing that this matter is of great importance, scheduled a meeting for April 2nd, convening representatives from various industries,

and inviting Yu Peng and Director Feng and others to attend, requesting a reduction in the business tax

rate to 0.2%, which has been disapproved by the Ministry of Finance.

The Kunshan-Taicang Highway from Kunshan to Taicang has been completed and is scheduled to open on April 1st.

The Jiangsu Provincial Highway Administration specifically instructed Dong Shiqian, director of the Sujia Highway

Office, on the 27th to concurrently manage the Kuntai Road. The fare is set at

3 yuan in legal tender and 3 jiao for small baggage from Kunshan to Taicang. The entire line has a central station at Zhendong Farm.

Corrupt Official from Changshu Arrested in Suzhou

Jiang Kan, the former head of tooth tax in Changshu, embezzled 3,000 yuan of public funds and fled to

Suzhou. On the 27th, the county government received instructions from the Provincial Education Administration

to order the Public Security Bureau to arrest Jiang. Chief Zhu of the Second Section of the county government interrogated him once,

submitted a report to the province for instructions on how to handle the case, and at the same time sent Jiang to the Security Brigade

headquarters for temporary custody.

Changshu

Plans to Reconstruct City Gates

The six city gates here are still old-fashioned and very

narrow. Except for the southeast gates, which have had their barbicans demolished,

the others have not been changed. Currently, the authorities believe that the city gates are narrow, which is inconvenient

for traffic. They plan to rebuild the more important southeast gates according to the Suzhou Xinlumen

method, with double-ring arched gates, so that vehicles and pedestrians can enter and exit on separate paths.

Koreans Arrive for Sightseeing

Yesterday in the urban area, two foreigners wearing Chinese clothing

came to visit. At first, it was suspected that they were Japanese, but after police investigation,

they claimed to be Koreans. They came here for sightseeing and had no other intentions. Subsequently, the bureau dispatched police to accompany them for protection.

After a brief tour of the northern suburbs, they took a car and left Changshu for Kunshan. The bureau also notified

the Kunshan Public Security Bureau to be informed.

County Magistrate Goes to Capital for Training

The Ministry of Interior is holding a training institute for county and city administrators, gathering county magistrates from all over the country

to receive training in the capital. Chen Fu, the county magistrate of this county,

is in the first class and is allowed to report to Beijing on April 2nd. All county affairs

are entrusted to Secretary Xu Wei to handle in his absence.

Kunshan

Two Fires in One Day

The residence of a resident surnamed Li on Baihua Street in this county,

a spacious house, suddenly caught fire late at night on the 26th.

Instantly, raging flames soared into the sky, bursting through the roof. The family woke up in shock and immediately sounded the alarm for help.

The fire brigades in each district received the news and mobilized to extinguish the fire. However, it was quite far

from the river, and it was difficult to fetch water. For a time, it was impossible to put out the fire. As a result, the fire intensified, and Wang Youcai's account books, which were rented inside, were completely burned, and it spread to the neighboring Li family's

house. Also, at around 3 p.m. on the same day, a fire broke out on Shipijie Street in Xidamen,

burning down a large firewood shed.

Rehabilitating Opium Addicts in Batches

A total of 1,200 newly registered opium addicts in this county.

The head of the first department of the county government, Long Dengyun, will soon select younger ones and rehabilitate them in batches,

in order to comply with the directive to ban opium within a limited time.

Wuxi

Banks Implement Insurance for Rice

Wuxi Bank notified the rice and bean

trade association last winter, advocating for insurance on loans secured by rice, beans, grains, and miscellaneous items.

The rice industry reported this to the chamber of commerce, which invited the relevant storage facilities, rice mills, oil mills, flour mills, and other

industries to jointly discuss the matter. In principle, they did not object, but they believed that rice and grain loans

were different from other goods, and it was very difficult to handle. It was decided to discuss the matter again at the end of March of this year. Now that the deadline is approaching, the banking industry has

sent a letter urging the rice industry to finalize the measures as soon as possible. After several rounds of negotiations among the relevant industries,

it was ultimately determined that the rice, grain, and miscellaneous items in Wuxi are of a fluid nature and are different from the situation in other counties.

The various parties jointly sent a letter to the chamber of commerce to forward to the banking industry, requesting a postponement. However, the banking industry has decided to implement insurance

in accordance with its regulations starting on April 1st. If insurance is delayed, credit will be immediately suspended. However, the rice market in Wuxi

is the champion of the county's commerce. If the banking industry suspends credit, the impact will ripple throughout the county's entire commercial market. Therefore, the chamber of commerce is now adopting both parties' intentions and plans to make a final and effective

mediation.

Jiang Vessels Docking on the South Bank of Jiangyin

The Jiangyin County Chamber of Commerce previously believed that the fact that vessels navigating the Yangtze River did not dock in Jiangyin

was of great importance to the commerce of the county. It negotiated for the opening

of the coal mine company pier on the south bank to serve as a docking point for various vessels. A report was submitted to the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance, which dispatched personnel to conduct a detailed survey of the waterway, deemed it feasible, and approved docking.

At the same time, it was agreed with the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company that, starting this month, all Jiang vessels

carrying goods from Wuxi, Changzhou, and other places would dock and unload on the south bank of Jiangyin, with a trial period of six months.

Now, the stall vendors bureau believes that after docking in Jiangyin,

whether the business can improve depends on whether agricultural and industrial products from Wuxi, Changzhou, and Chengjiang three counties

can be transported by the bureau. Yesterday, it specifically sent letters to the chambers of commerce of Wuxi, Changzhou, and Chengjiang, requesting them to inform the various industries

and provide support.

The Zou Chengtai Rice Mill in Jiangjianshang outside the North Gate of this county and the Shanghai Yutai Rice Firm

were involved in a debt dispute, which implicated Chen Shitao, a judge in the civil division of this county's local court,

on suspicion of accepting bribes. The High Court dispatched Lu Wenqin, a prosecutor from the Wuxian Local

Court, to Wuxi to summon Zou Fuwei, Zou Songfan, Zou Jikang, Yang Shaoyun, and others for questioning, and released Judge Chen on bail. It was decided that a joint interrogation would be conducted again in Suzhou today (the 28th). Yesterday, Judge Chen had already been

dismissed by order of the Ministry of Justice and sent to Suzhou for interrogation.

Zhonghao's house in Tangwan to move her belongings, but was stopped by the Sun family. Subsequently, Sun

Xicheng, a lawyer, went to the countryside with Town Head Sun Liangchu and both parties' relatives to discuss

Qiangfen shall terminate their marital relationship from this day forward. 2. All of Lu Qiangfen's personal

Huaiyin

Tragic Incident of Vicious Dog Mauling

Meng Hanzi, a resident outside Beiyu in Wangying Town of this county,

has two sons, the elder being nine years old and the younger being three years old.

He works as a vegetable seller. Yesterday (the 23rd), Meng and his wife went out on business, leaving the two sons at home.

However, the younger son was suffering from scarlet fever and had a foul odor.

Unexpectedly, after Meng and his wife left, a vicious dog suddenly

entered the room, smelling the foul odor emanating from the younger son, and fiercely bit his face.

Because the child was small and severely injured, he died instantly. The elder son, seeing this, cried out in alarm,

and took a wooden stick to chase the dog away. Neighbors heard the cries and rushed over, but the dog had already disappeared.

Soon after, Meng's wife returned home first and asked what had happened. The elder son, fearing, dared not speak. Meng's

wife, heartbroken over the younger son's tragic death, accidentally hit the elder son's head with a stick,

leaving it bloody and mangled. He also died soon after. By the time Meng Hanzi returned home, his wife

had fled in fear of punishment. Within one household, two children died on the same day, and a wife was lost.

The situation was extremely tragic.

Farmer Hangs Himself Due to Poverty

Xu Chenglai, a farmer in the vicinity of Changgouji in the seventh district of Husi County,

is nearly fifty years old. He has a wife

and two children. Recently, due to the spring famine, life has been unsustainable. Xu, feeling that there was no hope for life,

hanged himself in his room behind his family's backs last night (the 22nd). Ding Changgeng, a resident of the same settlement, sold his three-year-old

youngest son to Xue Yongchao in Hunan Village as his son because he had no rice to cook, receiving eight yuan in foreign currency to make a living.
