Local News

Bank Acceptance Exchange Holds First General Meeting Yesterday 74

Thirty-Eight Member Institutions Approve Xinhua Bank's Admission

Total Acceptance Amount Reaches 30,495,000 Yuan

Regulations Stipulate the Types of Collateral and Rediscount Methods

The "Bank Acceptance Exchange," affiliated with the Shanghai Banking Association Joint Reserve Committee, has been established and commenced operations since the 16th of this month. Internal procedures have been completed, and member banks have fully subscribed to the acceptance fund. A first general meeting since its establishment was held at the Hong Kong Road Banking Club yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m. to report on the progress. More than thirty representatives from all member banks, including Wu Yunzhai, Sun Jingxi, Wang Boyuan, and Yang J眉i, attended. Chairman Li Fusun presided over the meeting. First, the chairman briefly described the establishment of the acceptance exchange and the need to develop a bill discounting system. Then, Zhu Boquan, the manager of the exchange, reported on the progress since its establishment and passed a motion to admit Xinhua Bank as a member bank of the Joint Reserve Committee. Details of the events are recorded below:

Chairman's Address

Chairman Li Fusun stated:

In the past, the financial organization in Shanghai

had many imperfections. The most important

deficiencies were the lack of a clearing house and

a bill discounting system. These shortcomings

caused the industry to experience various inconveniences. Therefore, the first task of this committee

after its establishment was to organize a clearing

house. The clearing house has already achieved some success. However, the development of a bill discounting system has not yet begun. Without a discounting system, the industry's capital cannot be used flexibly and smoothly. When the market is bad, funds that are usually loaned out become stagnant on the books and cannot circulate, often leading to difficulties in turnover. The current market stagnation and the reduced capital utilization capacity of the industry are due to the lack of a discounting system. To develop a discounting system, we must first develop discountable bills. If there are bills but no "discount

market" to allow holders to discount them at any time, the discounting function cannot be fully utilized. Therefore, we in the industry have decided to organize a "Bank Acceptance Exchange" ourselves to create a type of discountable bill. These bills are issued by member banks of the acceptance exchange and accepted by the exchange. The form is the same as ordinary "banker's acceptances." Our "acceptances" are secured by commercial paper already discounted by member banks and other assets. Once accepted, the exchange will establish a discounting trading method to allow industry members holding our acceptances to realize them at any time, creating a rudimentary "discount market." In this way, some of the funds loaned out by the industry, which were originally fixed assets, can now be replaced with our acceptances and become liquid assets.

At the same time, our acceptances are well-guaranteed and highly flexible. All industry members can use their surplus funds to discount them. Bills purchased through discounting can be stored to earn interest and can still be rediscounted to other industry members or rediscounted to the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank when necessary. The surplus funds paid out for discounting are no different from storing them in one's own vault. Even if the amount of operating reserves is slightly reduced, there is nothing to fear. Moreover, the interest rate on discounting is usually lower than ordinary interest rates. In the future, as discountable bills develop, the overall market interest rate can also be lowered, increasing the industry's liquid assets and appropriately reducing normal operating reserves. This indirectly increases the industry's capital utilization capacity, expands the industry's business, and increases the industry's operating profits. However, the most important thing is that our industry can fully utilize this power to support industry and commerce, so that industry and commerce can also benefit significantly. We sincerely hope that all industry members will use our "acceptances" to gradually revitalize the current stagnant situation and develop "discountable bills," "discount markets," and "rediscounting" simultaneously, creating a perfect discounting system. Regarding the establishment process of our exchange and the current undertakings, please listen to Manager Zhu's detailed report.

Member Banks

Next, Mr. Zhu Boquan reported that

the initial number of member banks was

thirty-four. Subsequently, four more banks joined, making a total of

thirty-eight. All thirty-eight member banks have now signed public

agreements. These thirty-eight member banks are also member

banks and clearing banks of the Joint Reserve Committee. The list is as follows: Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank, Four Banks Savings Association, Y盐业 Bank, Zhongfu Bank, Siming Bank, Jin Cheng Bank, Xinhua Bank, Continental Bank, Yongting Bank, China Industrial Bank, China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Jiangsu Bank, Guohua Bank, China Reclamation Bank, China Agricultural and Industrial Bank, Tonghe Bank, Women's Commercial and Savings Bank, China National Products Bank, Juxingcheng Bank, China Bank, Zhonghui Bank, China National Industrial Bank, China Enterprise Bank, Hengli Bank, Silk Industry Bank, Jiangsu and Zhejiang Bank, Zhongyi Trust Company, Zhejiang Local Bank, Sichuan Meifeng Bank, Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank, Yongda Bank, and Pudong Bank.

Acceptance Fund

The amount of bill acceptance fund subscribed

by member banks is proportional to each bank's paid-up

capital and total reserve fund. This subscribed

fund has now been fully paid up, totaling 7,623,750 yuan in national currency.

Total Acceptance Amount

The exchange's acceptance amount

for member banks is also proportional to each bank's paid-up

capital and total reserve fund. Each bank separately

establishes the acceptance amount with the exchange through acceptance agreements. These acceptance agreements have also been signed by all banks, with the total acceptance amount set at 30,495,000 yuan in national currency.

Types of Collateral

Among the collateral accepted by the exchange, there

is a category of various major domestic products. The

types of domestic products are currently provisionally limited to fifteen: rice, wheat, flour,

coarse grains, cotton, grey cloth, sugar, silk, cocoons, tea,

tobacco leaves, coal, iron, and paper.

Discount Methods

In order to facilitate the discounting of the

exchange's acceptances by various banks and

promote the development of a discount market, the exchange has formulated a temporary trading method for discounting. Any member bank wishing to buy or sell

the exchange's acceptances can notify the exchange of the amount and interest rate at a designated time each day. If the amounts and interest rates requested by both parties match, the exchange will notify both parties to complete the transaction procedures. If there are sellers but no buyers on a given day, the Joint Reserve

Committee can discount the entire amount at the specified discount rate. The minimum transaction amount is 50,000 yuan, and the interest rate is calculated at a certain number of fen per thousand yuan per day. If a discounting bank needs to, it can rediscount the bills to other banks or to the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank. The principle of the Bank of China, Bank of Communications, and the Central Bank handling rediscounting has been established, but the details are still under discussion. Furthermore, the accounting of the Joint Reserve Committee and the acceptance exchange is completely independent. The exchange's acceptances can also be discounted by the committee when necessary. Therefore, the committee's discount rate is also posted and announced daily.

Bill Format

The exchange's acceptances have recently been

printed and distributed to member banks for use.

The format of these acceptances is the same as ordinary "banker's acceptances." It is a three-part form. The left end is the issuing bank's stub, the right end is the acceptance application, and the middle part is the "acceptance." Issuing bank stub: branch number, amount, term, acceptor, issue date, acceptance date, maturity date, remarks. Acceptance application: "In accordance with the terms and conditions stated in our bank's acceptance agreement No. 〇 dated 〇〇 year 〇 month 〇 day of the Republic of China, we hereby apply for acceptance of banker's acceptance No. 〇 (Chinese characters) for the face amount of 〇〇 yuan in national currency, using the property and goods deposited by our bank with your exchange as collateral. Please accept the bill and return the original bill to us. Sincerely, 〇〇〇 of the Bank Acceptance Exchange, 〇〇 year 〇 month 〇 day." Acceptance bill: "Pay 〇〇〇 after 〇〇 days from the date of issue for the amount of 〇〇〇 national currency. To: Shanghai Bank Acceptance Exchange for verification and payment. Issuer: 〇〇〇, 〇〇 year 〇 month 〇 day of the Republic of China." "This bill has been accepted today and will be paid in full on the maturity date of 〇〇 year 〇 month 〇 day without fail. Acceptor: Bank Acceptance Exchange of the Shanghai Banking Association Joint Reserve Committee, Manager 〇〇〇, Director 〇〇〇, 〇〇 year 〇 month 〇 day of the Republic of China." The words "Banker's Acceptance" are printed in the middle.

New Outlets for Banks 75

Organizing Rural Lending Institutions

Shiye News Agency reports: Since the Ministry of Finance officially announced on November 4 last year that the banknotes of the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications would be legal tender, commercial banks have complied and ceased issuing banknotes. Their main business has largely become government bonds and mortgages. At the end of last year, they all had large surpluses. However, since the beginning of this year, the number of mortgages has decreased, resulting in a large concentration of cash within the banks, making it difficult to find outlets. As a result of repeated meetings and consultations, it was decided to jointly organize a large-scale rural lending institution to provide relief to rural areas and find outlets for cash. According to reporter inquiries, the banks have reached a consensus and plan to establish a head office in Shanghai and branch offices in various counties, cities, and villages based on actual needs. This plan is currently being actively pursued and will soon be realized.

Cotton Control Committee Purchases High-Quality American Cotton Seeds 76

Disinfected and Shipped to Various Provinces for Mass Propagation

The Cotton Control Committee of the National Economic Council, the Central Cotton Improvement Institute, and the Central Agricultural Experiment Institute of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce have been cooperating and, in the past three years, have jointly conducted large-scale regional trials of Chinese and American cotton varieties with twenty domestic agricultural institutions. The results showed that the American Si Zi Cotton No. 4 purebred has excellent yields. The yield per mu is more than 20% higher than existing American cotton varieties. It performs best in the provinces of North China. Its characteristics are numerous fruit branches, rich boll formation, early maturity, and superior quality, surpassing the old Tuo Zi Cotton Ai Zi Cotton and others. Last winter, the committee ordered twenty-one tons of this Si Zi cotton seed from the United States. After arriving in Shanghai at the beginning of this month, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau was entrusted with disinfection to prevent the introduction of insects and bacteria attached to the cotton seeds into the country. It is reported that the disinfection procedures have been completed, and the seeds have been delivered to the Railway Bureau to be shipped to Hebei, Henan, Shaanxi, Shanxi, Shandong, Jiangsu, and other provinces for proper propagation.

American Silk Industry Tycoon, Gan Li, Comes to China to Investigate the Silk Industry 81

Hosts a Banquet for Chinese and Foreign Silk Industry Professionals to Exchange Ideas the Day Before Yesterday 82

Leaves for Wuxi Yesterday Morning to Visit Silk Factories and Returns to Shanghai That Evening 83

The United States is the largest consumer of raw silk in the world. Its annual import of raw silk is over 500,000 dan, of which Japan supplies 450,000 dan, while our country, even in the prosperous year of the silk industry last year, only supplied over 20,000 dan. In the year before last, exports to the United States were less than 10,000 dan. Most of the raw silk imported by the United States is handled by the Gan Li Company, which holds an important position in the American silk industry. For example, the Raw Silk Exchange was initiated by Gan Li, the founder of the company, and the Raw Silk Importers Association was also founded by him. Two years ago, he also organized the International Silk Association to promote pure silk fabrics and expand the use of raw silk. Our country's silk industry groups donated 5,000 for publicity purposes. Mr. Gan Li, recognizing that our country is the birthplace of sericulture but that its production and quality are not what they used to be, has taken time out of his busy schedule to come to China for a field investigation. He arrived in Shanghai with his wife on the Chichibu Maru on the 25th of this month. Local silk industry leaders such as Xue Shou Xuan, Shen Hua Chen, Zhu Jing An, Miao Zhong Xiu, and Li Shu Chu welcomed him at the pier. The day before yesterday, Gan Li hosted a banquet at the Cathay Hotel, inviting over fifty Chinese and foreign silk industry professionals, including Shen Hua Chen and Miao Zhong Xiu, to exchange ideas in detail. Yesterday, Mr. and Mrs. Gan, at the invitation of Xue Shou Xuan of the Wuxi Yongtai Silk Factory, took an early train to Wuxi, accompanied by Mr. and Mrs. Miao Zhong Xiu and Xue Zu Kang, to visit the silk factory. They are scheduled to return to Shanghai by car at 5 p.m. to attend a public banquet hosted by the Shanghai Silk Industry Groups, the Commodity Inspection Bureau, and the Zhejiang Provincial Sales Promotion Committee. It is reported that Mr. Gan Li will leave Shanghai on the morning of the 30th.

Election of Individual Group of Taxpayers Association, Voting Completed Yesterday, Ballot Boxes Opened Today 84

Chairman Xu Jiqing Reports on the Investigation Process

Commercial and Native Place Groups Scheduled to Vote at the Beginning of Next Month

The election of individual members of the Chinese Ratepayers Association of the Shanghai International Settlement took place yesterday morning at the Association's office on Hong Kong Road. The ballots will be counted at the City Chamber of Commerce Hall this morning. The voting elections for the commercial and native place groups have been scheduled. Details are as follows:

Voting Election

Yesterday morning at 9 a.m., the voting

ceremony for the individual members group was held at the Association's office.

Geng Jiaji of the Shanghai Municipal Government,

Zhao Tiezhang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Office in Shanghai, Lin Meiyan of the Shanghai Special City Party Department, Jin Runxiang of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Hu Fengxiang of the Zhejiang Association, Zhang Yichen of the Citizens Federation, Ge Futian of the Nantong Native Place Association, Ren Nongxuan of the Wuxi Native Place Association, and others attended. After Chairman Xu Jiqing conducted the ceremony, he reported on the investigation process of the election and appointed Zhang Yichen, Hu Fengxiang, Ye Jiaxing, and Ren Nongxuan to guard the ballot boxes. After Geng Jiaji of the Municipal Government, Zhao Tiezhang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Lin Meiyan of the City Party Department sealed the ballot boxes, voting began.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Xu Jiqing's report on the election investigation

process briefly stated: "In addition to publishing

a notice to solicit taxpayers to come to the Association

to fill out forms, the Association also pre-filled

the investigation forms with the names of taxpayers based on the membership list from the previous session. Then, staff were sent out to investigate. If there were no changes, the old information was kept, and the taxpayers only needed to stamp the investigation form to prove it. If there were changes, new forms were filled out. As of December 31 of last year, a total of 7,487 old and new investigation forms were received. At the same time, 2,842 investigation forms were sent by various organizations, totaling 10,329. Before compiling the list, after removing duplicates and unqualified forms, there were actually 9,672 forms. After further investigation, it was found that four people had duplicates and three were deceased, leaving only 9,665 people. 9,665 ballots were issued. Furthermore, voters No. 376 and No. 941 were deceased, so the actual number issued was 9,663," and so on.

Ballots to be Counted Today

Voting for the individual members group was scheduled

to end at 5 p.m. yesterday.

At 9 a.m. today, the ballots will be counted

at the City Chamber of Commerce Hall. Personnel from the Municipal Government, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the City Party Department, and various organizations will be sent to supervise. The order of counting is recorded below.

Pay the highest respect to the national flag, party flag, and portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen.

Read Dr. Sun Yat-sen's will. Appoint twelve tellers and twelve counters.

Open the ballot boxes and report the total number of votes.

Report the names of the elected candidates. The group will elect twenty-seven representatives.

General Assembly

The commercial and native place groups are scheduled

to vote at the beginning of April. Each

group will elect twenty-seven representatives,

totaling eighty-one. A general assembly will be held in mid-April to report on the Association's affairs and elect five Chinese directors, six Chinese committee members, one land committee member, and twenty-seven executive committee members. An executive committee meeting will then be scheduled to elect three standing committee members, one chairman, and one vice-chairman.

Labor Bureau Election Fails Inspection: President Determined to Thoroughly Investigate 85

Re-election Procedures to be Entirely Restarted

Re-election Procedures to be Entirely Restarted

Regarding the scheduled by-election for foreign directors of the Public Concession's Labor Bureau, according to reliable information from the Labor Bureau's information department, the Norwegian Consul General and leading Consul Mr. Ayr have sent a letter to the Labor Bureau stating that the consulates of various countries in Shanghai believe that in the previous election this year, 323 ballots were inadvertently not included in the Board of Directors election report announced by the Labor Bureau on March 24th. Therefore, the election should be considered invalid. Mr. Ayr also announced that the Labor Bureau's Board of Directors election is scheduled for April 20th and 21st, Monday and Tuesday. Furthermore, he stated that the consuls' intention is that this by-election should restart all procedures, such as the nomination of candidates, in accordance with Article 18 of the Land Regulations. As a result, the Director-General of the Labor Bureau has issued a notice stipulating April 20th and 21st as the dates for the 1936 Labor Bureau Board of Directors election. Nomination papers for candidates must be submitted to the Director-General of the Labor Bureau no later than 12:00 noon on April 9th (Thursday). The previous Labor Bureau Notice No. 4679 should be declared revoked.

Furthermore, the Director-General of the Labor Bureau, Mr. Fessenden, was quite furious about the oversight in the previous election, which resulted in the omission of 323 votes. Yesterday, he specifically stated to others that he was determined to immediately conduct a thorough investigation to clarify the truth.

Special District Telephone Fee Notification to Users: Resolution of the Fifth Council Meeting 86

Fifth Resolution of the Council Meeting

The Special District Telephone Issue Committee convened its fifth council meeting yesterday at 3:00 PM. Over 20 people attended, including Lu Wenzhong, Yu Yaoqiu, Xu Boliang, Ren Nongxuan, Zhu Yangwu, Li Ao Kui, Zhang Xianfang, and Liu Zhongying. The meeting was chaired by Lu Wenzhong. Items for discussion: Based on letters from telephone users in various districts requesting instructions on this month's payment method, please discuss this issue so that instructions can be issued to the relevant departments. Resolution: Notify users that for this month's payment, regardless of basic or exceeded calls, each call will be charged three cents. We will allow the company to handle this. Implementing the association's position, canceling the basic call limit, and calculating all calls at three cents each. Contact public organizations to jointly promote this proposal. Resolution: Send a letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession to submit it for discussion at the General Assembly, and also send letters to the Ratepayers' Association of the Second Special District, the Citizens' Federation, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, local associations, the five exchange brokers' associations, and the Lawyers' Association to advocate for a unified position. Furthermore, send a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce urging them to promptly convene a general meeting of representatives from various industries to discuss how to deal with the telephone price increase proposal. Resolution: Passed. The Electrical Industry Association suggested three methods for dealing with the telephone price increase: First, organize opportunities to remove telephones, with industry associations handling this for users and individuals in various industries, and the Citizens' Association handling it for others. How should this be handled? Resolution: First, notify the industry associations and the Citizens' Association to handle the volunteer telephone removal survey forms and forward them to the association for verification.

Haiyun and Ingeren Collide in Huangpu River Yesterday 87

Both Vessels Sustained Damage

The "Haiyun" wheel, formerly known as the "Daffy," operated by the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, specializes in the Shanghai-to-Lianyungang (Haizhou) route. It arrived in Shanghai fully loaded with goods transported via the Longhai Railway yesterday morning at 5:30 AM, just as the Norwegian ship "Ingeren," chartered by the Kailan Mining Administration, was arriving from Qinhuangdao fully loaded with coal. The "Ingeren" was in front, and the "Haiyun" was behind, sailing in close succession. When they reached the vicinity of the fourth river channel near the Yangshupu Power Plant, they collided. The outer iron plates on the "Haiyun" wheel's port bow were dented, and the mast on the "Ingeren" ship's aft deck starboard side was broken, the railings were completely destroyed, and the iron plates were also damaged. After the accident, both parties stopped to observe each other before sailing to Yangjiadu and the China Wharf to dock. The "Haiyun" shipowner, Huang, immediately reported to the headquarters, and the Norwegian ship also reported to Kaiji. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company immediately sent Chief Engineer Cao Shoulian to the "Haiyun" first, and decided to go to the Norwegian ship for inspection. At the same time, they reported to the China United Ship Insurance Association, requesting them to send a surveyor to inspect the ship as soon as possible. The issue of responsibility will be discussed separately.

"Gonglai" Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday: Major Collision with "Haicheng" in Guangdong 88

Both Vessels Sustained Significant Damage

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Gonglai" wheel, weighing 2,705 tons, with a length of 320 feet, a width of 46 feet, a depth of 21 feet and 1 inch, a draft of 16 feet and 2 inches, two decks, a horsepower of 2,020, a steam pressure of 160, and a speed of 9.5 nautical miles per hour, was built in England in 1894. The vessel usually sailed the northern and southern oceans, also served as a training vessel for graduates of the Wusong Merchant Marine School. It had sailed from Guangdong back to Shanghai, carrying 6,000 bags of Cantonese sugar and other goods, with a considerable number of passengers. The "Gonglai" wheel had just left Bai'etan in Guangzhou, less than half an hour before it collided head-on with the "Haicheng" wheel.

Circumstances of the Collision

According to shipowner Gunker (a Russian), the "Gonglai" wheel left Guangzhou at 5:01 PM on the 17th of this month, but by 5:30 PM, the ship had not yet left Huangpu Port when the major accident occurred. At this time, there was fog in the port, and the shipowner was on duty (shipowners are responsible for navigation within the port). As the "Gonglai" wheel was proceeding, it encountered the Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Min-Yue class steamer "Haicheng" (3,600 tons), which was carrying a large quantity of cargo and passengers from Fujian to Guangzhou. The "Haicheng" wheel was fast and powerful, and when it met the "Gonglai" wheel, the heavy fog prevented them from avoiding each other in advance, resulting in the bow side of the "Gonglai" wheel colliding heavily with the midship section of the "Haicheng" wheel. Both sides sustained significant damage at the time.

"Gonglai" Suffers Two Breaches

After the collision between the "Gonglai" and "Haicheng" wheels, the outer iron plates of the "Gonglai" wheel's keel side were completely dented, and the ribs of the hull were also bent. In the forward hold on the port side, two large holes were breached, and the forward water tank immediately flooded. Furthermore, the anchor on the port side of the bow was shattered, demonstrating the violence of the collision and the extent of the damage to the "Gonglai" wheel. After the accident, the "Gonglai" immediately stopped, and the shipowner inspected the damage while also examining the damage to the "Haicheng".

"Haicheng" Seriously Damaged

When the "Haicheng" wheel collided heavily with the "Gonglai", it was unable to stop immediately. Due to its great speed, the "Haicheng" wheel was damaged from the midship engine room to the stern. A large hole was breached in the engine room, so the damage was more serious than that of the "Gonglai". The "Haicheng" had more cargo and passengers than the "Gonglai". After the accident, in addition to the shipowners meeting to inspect and certify each other, the "Haicheng" took measures to sail to the dock, unload the cargo and passengers, and then undergo major repairs after inspection by a surveyor.

"Gonglai" Arrives in Shanghai Yesterday

After the collision, the "Gonglai" was unable to sail, and the forward water tank was flooding, creating a dangerous situation. The shipowner urgently returned to the Guangzhou dock, first using cement and wooden boards to fill the two holes, and then pumping out the water that had entered the hold. As a result, the "Gonglai" was delayed in Guangzhou for another three days. It finally set sail for Shanghai on the morning of the 21st, and arrived at the Wusong estuary at 7:30 AM yesterday morning. It then sailed to Huazhan to unload sugar, and the shipowner reported the accident and the collision to the Bureau. At the same time, he notified the insurance company, requesting them to send personnel for inspection.

Repairs After Inspection

The "Gonglai" ship arrived in Shanghai and docked on the Jiangmian of Jinliyuan Wharf. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company sent Chief Engineer Cao Shoulian to inspect the ship and inquired with the shipowner, Guntker, about all the details of the collision. The "Gonglai" now requires major repairs, making it difficult to sail immediately. Today, it is still necessary to wait for the insurance company's surveyor to inspect the ship before a decision can be made on repairs. The extent of the damage to the "Haicheng" wheel has not yet been reported.

Hawkers in Hongkou Vegetable Market Also Actively Donate

According to the Central News Agency, after the fundraising campaign to buy airplanes for Chiang Kai-shek's birthday celebration began in Shanghai, the association received a letter from Wang Taikang and other hawkers in the Hongkou vegetable market, sending donations of 3 yuan, Zhou Guichu, Lin Liming, Zhang Qixiang, and Gao Miao Hou each donated 1 yuan, Cheng Laibao and Gao Shengde each donated 5 jiao, Zhu Mingqi and Zhang Jingwen each donated 4 jiao, Xu Minsheng, Pan Laohu, Zhou Rongsheng, Xu Qihe, Shi Aqing, Zhang Guorong, Wang Xianglin, Song Youshun, Zhang Haiming, Fu Xingchu, and Li Fulan each donated 2 jiao, Ye Fangzhong, Ma Jiahuai, Zhao Xiaomei, and Li Futing donated 1 jiao, and Liu Dinghua and Xia Jiming donated 5 fen, totaling 11 yuan, 4 jiao and 2 fen in national currency. The original letter stated, "Having read in the newspapers that this year is the 50th birthday of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, who has worked tirelessly and made great contributions, and that preparations are underway to purchase ten airplanes to celebrate his birthday as a sign of respect, we, although small hawkers in the Hongkou vegetable market, are no less patriotic and respectful of the leader. We are donating our spare change for the purchase of airplanes. Please accept this." Although these hawkers are hardworking and have limited income, their patriotic enthusiasm and willingness to save money to donate is truly commendable. The committee, after jointly inviting leaders from all circles, organizations, and institutions in the city as initiators, has been receiving letters of acceptance every day, which is very encouraging. Furthermore, the association received a letter yesterday from Cheng Weiqin, Guo Lianggao, Chen Zaiyi, Chen Youbin, and Zou Zhiming of the Zhongshan Warship, sending 6 jiao in stamps for the purchase of airplanes for the birthday celebration, which shows the enthusiastic support of compatriots across the country.

China International Famine Relief Commission: Relief Work in the Past Six Months 92

Total Relief Funds Amount to Over 190,000 Yuan

The China International Famine Relief Commission, located at 505 Henan Road in Shanghai, recognizing the severity of last summer's floods, specially obtained approval from the Ministry of Interior to carry out river flood relief work, raise relief funds, and provide relief to the disaster victims. From August last year to the end of February this year, a total of 190,382.50 yuan in national currency was used for work relief and emergency relief. The relief area covers 58 counties in Shandong, Jiangsu, Henan, Hebei, Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Fujian provinces. Among them, the work relief in northern Jiangsu, repairing the Xuzhou-Haizhou highway and the lake embankment, required the most funds, totaling more than 50,000 yuan. It was decided to dredge the Quanhe River in Wenshang County, Shandong, and 25,000 yuan in national currency and 1,000 bags of flour were allocated. The emergency relief was mainly distributed in Jining, Jinan, Yanzhou, De County, Longshan, Zhen County, Yi County, Zou County, Linqing, Tai'an in Shandong, Suqian, Xuzhou, Haizhou in Jiangsu, and Yanshi and Huaiqing in Henan.

China International Famine Relief Commission: Reported Tragic Famine Situation in Huoqiu 93

The drought in northwestern Anhui Province has become increasingly severe since spring, with Huoqiu in western Anhui being the most tragic. Yesterday, Mr. Chen Shifu, a representative from the county, arrived at the China International Famine Relief Commission on Renji Road in Shanghai, having traveled a long distance to personally beg for relief. He brought photos of the disaster victims and five kinds of food for survival: sorghum bran, sorghum lees, locust fruit, elm bark flour, and sesame cakes. He said that dozens of people are starving to death every day. The representative is the chairman of the Huoqiu County Early Disaster Relief Association, is already old, and his beard is almost reaching his chest. He almost cried as he spoke of the various aspects of the disaster, which is imaginable. He also presented a letter from County Magistrate Wei Liren, which is transcribed as follows: "The drought last summer was extremely severe, and the entire county, whether fertile or barren, was a barren land. The warehouses are empty, and the people's food is exhausted. Since the spring, there has been rain and snow, and the cold wind has been strong. The disaster victims who are displaced and wandering have no way to meet their basic needs of clothing, food, housing, and transportation. They stumble and fall, and the dead are seen on the roads. According to a recent survey, during the Lantern Festival and around February 2nd, dozens of people were starving to death on the outskirts of the city because they had no way to beg for food due to the heavy snow. More than a dozen cases are also reported daily inside and outside the city gates. Changtangshao, Chalu Kou, Lianhua Temple, and Wolong Temple in the south of the county are the most affected. It is also reported that some people are eating human flesh. The starving people fill the streets, their faces are haggard, and they are on the verge of death. The old, weak, and disabled are huddled in the mud, lying there stiff and slanting. People who pass by their side hear them call for help, which is unbearable to hear. This is truly a rare disaster unseen in nearly a hundred years. There are still a hundred days before the wheat harvest. How can we endure the long night? We have specially appointed Chairman Chen Shifu to bring photos of the disaster and personally present the disaster situation, and to request a large amount of relief funds to save the spring famine and protect the lives of the people." It is reported that the association has decided to allocate 20,000 yuan and is setting up a branch in Yingshang to carry out relief work for the disaster victims in the eight counties of northwestern Anhui Province. However, the disaster is severe and the funds are limited. We hope that all circles will be aroused and provide full assistance to save more lives.

Shanghai International Exhibition: Exhibits Shipped to Shanghai 94

Over Seventy Leaders from Chinese and Foreign Circles Support

The Industrial Federation Notifies All Members Nationwide to Actively Participate

The Shanghai International Exhibition, since being supported by leaders from all walks of life such as Du Yuesheng, Yu Zuoting, and Lin Kanghou, has been progressing smoothly. Many manufacturers of national goods from various provinces and cities have sent letters requesting to participate in the exhibition. The construction of the venue has begun, and Chinese and foreign exhibits will be shipped to Shanghai one after another. It is predicted that the opening on July 1st will be a sensation. The latest developments of the association are recorded as follows:

Enthusiastic Support from Leaders of All Circles

Leaders from Chinese and foreign business circles in Shanghai, recognizing that the market in Shanghai has been far from what it was since January 28th, which has had a significant impact on the social economy, pooled funds six months ago to prepare for the Shanghai International Exhibition, hoping to revitalize the declining market. With the support of Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Du Yuesheng, Chairman of the China Remittance Bank, Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Bankers' Association, and various industrial and commercial organizations, the association's work has progressed very smoothly. Foreign businesses in Shanghai have also expressed their approval. Currently, the association has received letters of support from various parties, with over seventy people agreeing to serve as supporters.

Active Participation of Manufacturers Nationwide

The China General Federation of Industrial Associations, as well as manufacturers of national goods, have expressed their approval of the association's purpose and plan to set aside a large space in the venue to display national goods products to promote them. They have sent letters to all members nationwide, selecting exquisite products to participate in the exhibition, so that visitors can see the excellent quality of national goods in recent years and compete to buy them, which will surely lead to a significant improvement in sales.

Exhibits Shipped to Shanghai

As for the recent preparations of the association, according to the preparations staff, the venue layout can be roughly divided into three parts: the exhibition area, the entertainment area, and the commercial area. The exhibition area will collect excellent items from various countries, displaying them in one place, such as antiques, machinery, literature, embroidery, crafts, and so on, with everything that should be there. More attention will be paid to exquisite domestic products and specialty products from various provinces and cities to promote them. Excellent imported goods will also be collected and displayed for Chinese people to observe. The commercial area construction will build large stores for merchants to rent. The store buildings are new and magnificent, with over 700 stores in various styles. All layouts strive for artistry. The rent for each store is over 400 yuan for two months. The association will soon publish a large number of advertisements to solicit tenants. As for Chinese and foreign exhibits, they have been shipped to Shanghai one after another.

Venue Layout Underway

The various preparations for the entertainment area are also being handled separately. The main ones include a zoo, collecting rare birds and animals from around the world; a man-made ice rink, providing visitors with ice skating to escape the summer heat during the hot season, which is a first in Shanghai; a swimming pool, a dance hall, a martial arts arena, Chinese and foreign theaters, mechanical games, and so on. To increase visitors' interest, the association has also decided to hire as many people as possible to join the entertainment area.

Directory of National Import and Export Firms 97

Scheduled to be Published in Mid-April

The International Trade Bureau, for the convenience of import and export merchants and the reference of the financial community, has compiled a directory of national import and export firms in both Chinese and English. It took a year, and staff were sent to Beijing, Tianjin, Ping, Shanghai, Wuhan, Min, Yue, Qing and other important commercial ports for on-the-spot investigations, collecting import and export firms from China and abroad, a total of 1,128. The contents are divided into name, address, telegraph and telephone number, date of establishment, situation of head office and branches, main and important commodities and businesses operated, and the banks and firms of the manager are also listed. The firms have been pre-ordering and advertising. The whole book is scheduled to be published in mid-April. If you need to place advertisements, please submit them to the Bureau at 1040 Suzhou Road before April 5th.

In addition to contacting the road bureaus for travel arrangements, as soon as everything is ready, the regulations will be drafted and published in the newspaper to start registration. [3] In the border area between Xiuning and Qimen counties in our hometown, the remnants of bandits are still rampant, and the people are not safe. It was decided to compile the recent bandit situation in each county into intelligence, inform the fellow-townsmen in various places, and send a telegram to Commander-in-Chief Zhang Fakui, ordering the local troops to vigorously suppress the bandits and eliminate them.

The Post Office Robbery Case Appeal Result: Monk Wukong Sentenced to Death; Monk Disagrees with Original Sentence, Appeal Rejected 99

Last September 9th, the thieving monk Wukong (also known as Ji Rentang) led a gang armed with weapons to break into the General Post Office on North Sichuan Road, robbing the bureau of over 90,000 yuan in banknotes and coins destined for the Savings and Remittance Bureau. They also shot and killed the escorting personnel. After the incident, they fled to Funing, Jiangbei. Subsequently, the police sent detectives who successively arrested several of his accomplices. After interrogation by the First Special District Court, they were found guilty and sentenced accordingly. The thieving monk, dissatisfied with his life sentence, appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The Municipal Council, however, argued that the thieving monk was the ringleader and should be executed according to the law. The initial sentence of life imprisonment was insufficient to deter others. Therefore, they also filed an appeal, requesting a death sentence. The Second Branch of the High Court, presided over by Judge Yu of the Criminal Division, specially convened a collegiate bench to finalize the interrogation. Yesterday afternoon, they ordered the thieving monk to be brought to court to pronounce the verdict, overturning the original sentence and changing it to a death sentence. The thieving monk's appeal was rejected. After the verdict, he was ordered to be returned to custody, pending confirmation and submission to the Ministry for approval before execution.

Vegetable Vendors on Zhabei Sanlu Road Request City Government Approval to Set Up Stalls 102

According to the Ta Kung Press, one hundred and forty-four vegetable vendors from the Sanyang Road area in Zhabei, including Cao Asi, Sun Shuangshou, Tao Chengshan, Pan Zhenghe, and Sun Afu, petitioned the Municipal Party Headquarters yesterday, requesting that the City Government be consulted to allow them to set up stalls to make a living. Their joint petition stated: "We, the undersigned, jointly petition that, without the City Government's approval, our livelihoods are on the verge of collapse, and we are facing imminent death, causing widespread panic. We earnestly request relief to maintain the people's livelihood. We citizens, young and old, have come from afar to Shanghai to seek a livelihood. Unfortunately, we encountered the Shanghai war, so we are still at risk of starvation. We were able to reach our present state thanks to the loan capital provided by the refugee relief center in the war zone. As a result, we were saved from fire and water and became small vegetable vendors, barely surviving. Unexpectedly, last winter, the manager surnamed Deng of the newly built vegetable market on Yanjia Ge Road, without considering the circumstances or respecting the law, due to the sluggish market, unexpectedly led gangsters to Sanyang Road, driving us citizens to the vegetable market to set up stalls and do business. We believe that as poor people seeking a living, we have not committed any illegal acts. Although the City Government has not explicitly approved it, the Finance Bureau directly under the City Government has been collecting donations monthly for several years. This shows the government's indirect approval. Even if the road is opened and stalls are prohibited, the administrative authorities should announce it to the public so that the ban can be enforced within a time limit. Moreover, the Deng surname's private vegetable market belongs to merchants, so how can they prohibit us without authorization? If they were acting on orders, they should bring official documents to facilitate enforcement. Otherwise, it is impossible to accept their orders. The Deng surname, feeling unjustified, left without a word. The next day, he intensified his actions, bringing trucks and arresting hundreds of vendors, sending them to the North Station Branch for investigation. The bureau chief, without distinguishing right from wrong, immediately detained us, causing us pain. Therefore, we jointly submit this petition to your department, requesting that you consult the City Government to allow us to set up stalls temporarily to maintain the livelihoods of thousands of poor people. We earnestly request that you consider the situation and provide appropriate relief."

Gu Zhuxuan and Wang YuGao were convicted of inciting murder. The Second Special Court sentenced Gu to 15 years imprisonment, and Wang to life imprisonment. Gu and Wang, dissatisfied, appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. The overseers Ma Xianxiang, Ma Xiancai, and Wang Yushou fled with the money. After the Second Special Court Prosecutor Wang questioned them clearly, he filed a public prosecution with the Criminal Division of the same court. Judge Li Changnian questioned the various details, as reported in the previous newspaper. Yesterday afternoon at 2:30 PM, Third Branch of the High Court Judge Wang Yue opened the Fifth Investigation Court to investigate the accuser Zhang Tinggui, also known as Zhang Xiaosizi. The official asked Wang Xinggao if he knew him. Zhang replied that he did not know him, but only knew Wang Jinkui. When asked what Wang Jinkui looked like, he replied that he was shorter than me and had a dark complexion. When asked if there was such a thing as a bank savings passbook, he replied that there was. When asked who spoke to him about it first, he replied that it was the overseer Wang Yushou. When asked what he said, he replied that he said that he and Zhao Guangfu had already made arrangements and asked me to recant my testimony in the appellate court. At that time, I refused. Later, the overseer Ma Xianxiang came to me and told me about Gu Zhuxuan's case, saying that the police and the court had all been taken care of, and it was useless for me to bite him alone, so I should be a good person and take some money to use. Zhao Guangfu had already received 4,000 yuan. At this point, I agreed. I asked him how much money it was. He said 3,000 yuan, and he wanted a 500 yuan commission, so I would only get 2,500 yuan. At that time, I said to Ma that I had to have evidence before I could recant my testimony. Ma immediately agreed to deposit the money in the bank. I asked him whose account it was. He said that it could not be in my name, but in the name of Wang Chunhua. I replied that was fine. Later, on the day of the hearing, Ma showed me the deposit book outside the prison gate. Because it was too far away, I could not grab it. On January 4th (the date of Gu's appeal hearing) at 6 AM, Ma brought the deposit book again for me to look at. At this point, I grabbed the deposit book and inspected it. There was only 2,000 yuan in the account. When I asked him where the other 500 yuan was, he said that after the court session today, he would go to Gu's house tomorrow to get the money and seal and bring it to you. Ma also said that when you go to court today, you only need to say that Zhao Guangfu told you to come out to testify, but this deposit book cannot be kept by you, but must be kept by a third party. So, I gave it to Cao Shida, a fellow prisoner, for safekeeping. On the sixth, Ma Xianxiang and others took the remaining money and seal and fled. Therefore, I filed a complaint with the Third High Court.

The court ordered Zhang to be returned to custody.

Commodity Inspection Bureau Convenes a Discussion Meeting Yesterday 110

Stipulating the Quantity of Yellow Dye to Be Purchased in Various Regions

The Bureau Will Dispatch Personnel to Investigate and Guide Further Research

According to the Industry and Commerce News Agency, the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, considering that the late spring season is approaching and new tea will soon be on the market, and in order to promote the improved yellow dye, convened a discussion meeting yesterday afternoon at 2 PM in the Bureau's conference room at New Garbage Bridge, gathering tea merchants from the city. In attendance were Bureau Chief Cai Wuji, Senior Technicians Wu Juenong and Zhou Zhenjun, as well as representatives from the Tea Manufacturing Trade Association Huang Zuyin, Peng Zhiping, Zheng Jianshen, and Yu Jinming, and representatives from the Tea Guild Hall Sun Zifu and Zhuo Huapu. Chairman Cai Wuji opened the meeting and briefly stated the purpose of the meeting, saying that the Yellow Dye Factory has not yet completed its contract and that merchants have been recruited to manage it. The goods already produced cannot be forcibly purchased. Therefore, the Tea Manufacturing Trade Association's request to recruit merchants to manage it separately is inconsistent with the original contract and should continue to be processed. He hoped that everyone would express their opinions to facilitate discussion on how to promote it in the future. Subsequently, Wu Juenong reported that, according to the sales quantity report of the Yellow Dye Factory, over 22,000 catties were sold in 1934, but less than 6,000 catties were sold in 1935. The reason why sales were not maximized in 1935 was that many tea companies did not help promote it. The Bureau had originally planned to have tea companies submit samples for inspection and register inland tea companies, and foreign merchants also hoped to inspect the tea before purchasing it. However, the Bureau, at the request of the tea companies, also believed that the blame for the coloring lay in the fact that the inland tea companies had not yet understood the truth, and it would be difficult to achieve universality without dispatching personnel for on-site guidance. However, the tea companies' inability to assist also created great difficulties in the process. Then, the discussion began on the method of promoting the yellow dye.

(Resolved) (A) It is stipulated that each household in Shanghai, Wenzhou, and Pingshui must purchase at least one dan, each household in Tunxi Yushan must purchase at least half a dan, and each household in Wuyuan and Suian must purchase at least twenty catties. Except for Yushan, which will be directly contacted by the Bureau to the county government, ordering tea companies to purchase it, the rest of the places will be distributed by each tea company to each household for trial use. If the trial use is not very satisfactory, each tea company or tea house can directly contact the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau for improvement. (B) Each tea company should be responsible for urging each tea house to purchase and use it, and the Bureau will send personnel to various places for investigation and guidance at any time. (C) The Bureau will invite Technician Tu to continue research. The meeting adjourned around 4 PM.

工部 Discusses Reducing Rickshaw Rental Fees: Rickshaw Businessmen Hold General Meeting Yesterday 111

Unanimous Resolution to Oppose

Rickshaw businessmen in this city, in order to oppose the reduction of rickshaw rental fees, held a general meeting of vehicle owners at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday morning at 9:00 AM. More than 800 people attended, including Mao Guibao, Zhao Fengshan, Wang Kunyi, Yin Zhiling, Gu Songmao, Qin Zhihui, Ni Yuebo, Hou Shao'an, Lu Dexin, Zheng Jian San, Jiang Caicheng, Yin Zhifang, Bao Zhenhuang, Qiu Jixiang, Hu Hongxue, and Ding Youpeng. Mao Yun from the Municipal Party Headquarters and Li Ruzhang from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce were dispatched to provide guidance. The presidium consisted of Yin Zhiling, Gu Songmao, Hou Shao'an, Wang Kunyi, and Song Shixiang. The meeting commenced with customary rituals, beginning with Chairman Yin Zhiling reporting the purpose of the meeting. Subsequently, representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce delivered speeches.

Immediately after, the discussion began, and the following resolutions were passed:

The Shanghai Municipal Council, based on the recommendation of the Rickshaw Committee, intends to further reduce rickshaw rental fees by eight cents starting from April 1st, violating the agreement reached on August 6, 1934. How should we respond to this? (Resolution) Unanimously opposed and passed.

The Shanghai Municipal Council unilaterally abolishes the August 6th Agreement and separately stipulates a daily rickshaw rental fee of seventy cents and a mandatory mutual aid fee of seven cents. How should we express our position on this? Resolution: (A) Public concession rickshaws are licensed by the Chinese, French, and British areas. The Shanghai Municipal Council should not overstep its authority to stipulate rickshaw rental fees, as this concerns national sovereignty and the regulations of various jurisdictions. This association finds it difficult to comply. (B) The Shanghai Municipal Council has the right to regulate passenger fares for public transportation businesses. However, the relationship between rickshaw owners and rickshaw pullers is a lease, which is not comparable to passengers and public buses. Therefore, the Shanghai Municipal Council should not interfere with the rent agreements agreed upon by both rickshaw owners and pullers.

The Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association is purely a Chinese labor union and a mass organization. It should be guided by the Chinese Party Headquarters and not be taken over by foreigners. This concerns national sovereignty over the guidance of the people. Letters should be sent to the Shanghai Municipal Council for negotiation and submitted to the Municipal Government and the Municipal Party Headquarters for rectification. Furthermore, assistance in negotiation should be requested from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Ratepayers Association.

A letter from rickshaw puller representatives states that they will refuse to pay the mutual aid fee starting in April. How should this be handled? Resolution: (A) Send a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council requesting their attention. (B) Based on the obligation of each vehicle owner to collect and pay on behalf, since the payers have already declared a suspension of payment, this association will temporarily suspend payment on behalf until the payers re-express their intention to continue payment.

Donation and license fees for April: Resolution: Each vehicle owner should, before March 31st, deposit two yuan and nine cents per license at the bank designated by this association, awaiting negotiation and resolution for collective donation of licenses to show solidarity.

Rickshaw puller registration: The Rickshaw Committee disregards the agreement and arbitrarily restricts rickshaw puller registration, leading to the unemployment of more than 20,000 rickshaw pullers. For the past few months, each vehicle owner has been trying to maintain their livelihood. How should this be handled? Resolution: The Shanghai Municipal Council should be requested to register them as soon as possible so that they can pull rickshaws for a living, maintaining business and stabilizing society.

New rickshaw design modification proposal: Resolution: The new rickshaw design has been trialed for a year, and the results are poor. The Shanghai Municipal Council should be requested to modify and adopt it based on public vehicle standards to meet the needs of public vehicles.

The meeting adjourned after the discussions. A declaration was issued, the text of which is omitted for brevity.

Searching for Husband for Thirteen Years: Meeting Leads to New Love for Him. Plaintiff's Lawyer States Similar to Meng Jiangnu's Long Journey to Find Husband. Nan Asks for Mediation on Cohabitation and Monthly Alimony. 112

Wu Wang, a woman from Fujian, recently engaged lawyer Jia Yaoxi to file a lawsuit in the Second Special Court's Civil Division, accusing her husband, Wu Fuguan (currently residing at No. 42, Fengyu Lane, Sapse Road), of bigamy, adultery, and abandonment. She requested mediation. The gist of her lawsuit is as follows: The petitioner married the defendant in her hometown at the age of seventeen. At that time, the couple's feelings were very good. Because they were childless, they adopted Wu Gengmin as their son according to Fujian custom. He is now fifteen years old. When Gengmin was one year old, the defendant left home to do business and borrowed several hundred yuan from his mother to go to Shanghai. Since then, he has never returned, disappearing without a trace for thirteen years. During this time, the petitioner brought her son to Shanghai several times, leaving her hometown and enduring hardships in search of him, but to no avail. It was not until last winter that a fellow villager pointed out the defendant's residence. She then learned that the defendant had a formal new lover in Shanghai. After entering the house, she was confined to the attic and treated like a servant. The defendant often spoke harshly and quarreled with her. When he was occasionally displeased, he would insult her indirectly and mock her coldly and sarcastically, indicating a complete break in their relationship. It is undeniable that the law stipulates that a married couple should have only one husband and one wife, and they have a mutual obligation to cohabit. Now that the defendant has taken another lover and disregards his first wife, and after thirteen years, abandons her like worn shoes upon reunion, she requests that the case be summoned for mediation, ordering the defendant to sever his relationship with his new lover immediately, resume cohabitation with the petitioner, and pay monthly alimony of 200 yuan. At the same time, she requests permission to reserve the petitioner's right to criminally prosecute the defendant for abandonment and bigamy.

Yesterday afternoon, the court summoned them. First, the petitioner's lawyer stated the past events, saying that the defendant's business in Shanghai is very good, accumulating assets of hundreds of thousands of gold, yet his wife is like Meng Jiangnu, who traveled thousands of miles to find her husband, but was abandoned after reunion. He asked for a fair judgment. The defendant did not appear. Lawyer Xi Shichang stated that the defendant could agree to cohabitation, but could not accept the other conditions. As for the current cohabiting woman, she is in the status of a concubine. Judge Guo instructed that the mediation was unsuccessful, and the petitioner should file another lawsuit.

Lawyers Association Submits to the Land Court, Requesting Improvement in Reporting and Execution Procedures 113

The Shanghai Lawyers Association submitted a document to the Shanghai Land Court yesterday, stating that it was submitting the document to improve the procedures for pre-trial reporting, in-court rescheduling, and execution of seizures and appraisals, following the procedures of the Shanghai First Special District Land Court. According to a proposal by member Xu Zuoliang, "The Shanghai First Special District Land Court has improved procedures for parties to report for pre-trial hearings. Parties report to the court during the hearing, and if the court deems it necessary to reschedule, it designates a date in court and no longer issues summonses to parties who have already reported. Also, execution of seizure cases often involves the clerk executing two or three cases on the same day. When seizing real estate worth less than 100 yuan, the clerk and bailiff immediately appraise the value. This method has been practiced for a long time without any hindrance or abuse. The Shanghai Land Court should follow suit to save time and other procedures. This is analyzed and explained below: Reporting in court can save the time of the bailiff on duty handling the execution. The judge can also observe whether the parties have arrived on time. Designating a retrial date in court can save the procedures and time for drafting and serving summonses, and it can also allow the parties who have arrived to prepare in advance, making it convenient for them to travel far or arrive on time. The reason why seizure events are time-consuming is often due to the debtor's reconciliation or hesitation in raising funds. To save time, the courts in the First and Second Special Districts require a dedicated clerk to schedule one or two cases with nearby addresses on the same date for joint execution. For example, in Case A, the debtor of Case A is kept at the debtor's premises to reconcile with the creditor or order the debtor to raise funds, and handle procedures such as checking property. At the same time, go to the debtor of Case B and do the same. Then go to the debtor of the inner case. Finally, return to Case B and Case A to see how they are raising funds or reconciling. If there is no way, the bailiff has completed all the seizure procedures, and the clerk can immediately supervise the seizure. Time and legal facts are not hindered. When the amount seized is less than 100 yuan, the appraisal is done on the same day to avoid delaying the date due to the appraisal, which will harm both the creditor and the debtor. The principle is very clear. It is requested that the Shanghai Land Court immediately adopt and improve the procedures to facilitate litigation." The resolution of the Joint Meeting of the 220th Executive Supervisory Committee of the Association was to forward it to your court for approval and implementation. It is a public convenience.

Page 14

Traveling Around the World: British Giant Ship Arrives in Shanghai 114

Carrying an American Travel Group of 387 People; After Landing, More Than 100 Cars Take to See Shanghai

The "Queen Empress," a giant ship of the British Chang Dian Company circumnavigating the globe, arrived in Shanghai at 1:55 PM yesterday and berthed in the waters of Sanjia, outside the Wusongkou. The American travel group traveling on the ship, a total of 387 people, transferred to the company's passenger ship at 4:05 PM and landed at the new customs pier. One hundred and seven Yunfei cars took them on a tour of the city and the downtown area. Except for twelve people who stayed in Shanghai to take the train to Peiping, the rest returned to the original ship, scheduled to sail to Qinhuangdao at 11:00 AM today.

Delayed Due to Fog, Anchored at Sanjia

The ship departed from New York on January 13th, crossing the Atlantic Ocean and passing through the Maltese Islands, Bombay, Colombo, Penang, Bangkok, Singapore, Java, and Luzon. It arrived in Hong Kong on the 24th of this month and continued sailing to Shanghai the next day. Changxing Company received a telegram from the ship the day before, saying that it would arrive in Shanghai at 6:00 AM yesterday, so the company set off from the new customs pier at 4:30 AM yesterday with two passenger ships, "Alexander" and "Smith," and sailed to Wusongkou. A reporter from the East China News Agency rushed to the new customs pier at night to board the Smith to visit and take news photos (see circle). When the reporter arrived at the pier at 4:00 AM, it was drizzling. The two passenger ships set off on time and arrived at the sea off Wusongkou at 5:40 AM. The sky was already dawning, but there was no sign of the "Queen Empress". The British manager and Chinese director Li Quan of Changxing Company instructed the shipowner to continue forward, and arrived at the waters of Sanjia at 6:15 AM, but still no trace. So at 6:20 AM, they sailed back to Wusong and wired the company to inquire, only to learn that the "Queen Empress" had encountered fog midway and would arrive at 2:30 PM. Everyone then looked for a way to land and rest. The two passenger ships also waited on the Jiangmian River at the Quarantine Office.

Group Members Land and Tour Shanghai

At 1:00 PM, the two passenger ships set off again to the outside of the mouth. At 1:40 PM, the giant ship appeared in front of them and anchored at Sanjia waters at 1:55 PM. After the passenger ship docked with the giant ship, the police chief of the Public Security Bureau boarded the ship to check passports. Then, the members of the travel group, a total of 387 people, and seven other passengers, who were traveling around the world on the giant ship, stepped into the small boat to Shanghai. When they arrived at the new customs pier at 4:05 PM, they changed to 107 Yunfei cars parked outside the door and drove away one after another.

Tea Dance at the Cathay Hotel

A row of cars went in two lanes. Fifty of them went to Nanshi, Yimiao, the French Concession, Zhaofeng Garden, and the Zhabei city street, directly to the downtown area, to visit the new Shanghai buildings. Fifty-seven of them went to the downtown area first, then to Zhabei, Zhaofeng Garden, and then to the city. At 6:00 PM, they returned to the Cathay Hotel. At 7:00 PM, they had dinner at the hotel. At 9:00 PM, Chang and Company specially hosted a tea dance at the Cathay Hotel ballroom to entertain all the members.

Leaving Shanghai for Qinhuangdao This Afternoon

The tea dance ended at 10:30 PM with joy. A part of the members boarded the Smith passenger ship, which set off from the new customs at 11:00 PM, to return to the original ship. Twelve people opened rooms at the Cathay Hotel to stay in Shanghai, waiting to take the Shanghai-Peiping train, which departed at 4:00 PM this afternoon, to Peiping. The rest of the members returned to the original ship by passenger ship at 2:00 AM and 8:30 AM this morning. According to Li Quan of Changxing Company, the "Queen Empress" is scheduled to leave Shanghai at 11:00 AM today (28th) and sail to Qinhuangdao, passing through famous cities in various countries, including Qinhuangdao, Osaka, Kobe, Yokohama, Wenwo, San Francisco, Honolulu, Los Angeles, Havana, and other ports, and returning to New York around the 14th of next month.

The Whole Ship is Exquisitely Constructed

Li Quan of the East China News Agency, under the guidance of Li Quan of Chang Company, once boarded the ship to visit for a week. The ship's appearance is white, and the three smokestacks are orange-yellow. The part below the waterline is green. The ship is 1,050 feet high, and looks like a 15-story building when viewed from below. According to Li, this ship was built in 1930 and was launched by Queen Mary of England. This is the second time it has come to China. The first time it crossed China was last spring. The ship is 759 feet long, 97.5 feet wide, has a displacement of 63,750 tons, and a load of 42,500 tons. It is equipped with three engines, which can generate 64,400 horsepower at the same time. The speed is 24.5 nautical miles per hour. Sailing on the ocean, it is not afraid of hurricanes and huge waves. The whole ship has a total of eleven floors. From the lowest floor to the eighth floor, there are three elevators. The ninth floor has two sports fields and tennis courts, as well as a cinema, music room, gym, barber shop, medical room, beauty salon, children's playground, and other facilities, which are very exquisite. You can ride a bicycle freely in the corridors of the ship. The greatness of the construction can be seen from this.

People and Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association Hospital to Open

The Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers Mutual Aid Association has been established for more than a year, and its efforts in service have long been praised by the public. The association has established five clinics for members and their families who are ill (the number of Western medicine diagnoses in the past was 130,422, and the number of Chinese medicine diagnoses was 112,212). Now it has created another hospital, the interior of which has been prepared and is scheduled to open on April 1. In addition, the association's general mutual aid provides rice to 903 cases (one liter per day for adults, eight he for children), funeral expenses to 101 cases (from 20 yuan to 30 yuan per case), travel expenses to 163 cases (average of 5 yuan per case), small capital loans to 9 parts (from 2 yuan to 8 yuan per case), housing money to 5 parts (average of 2 yuan per case), and food to 73 cases (average of 1 yuan per case), and clothes to 1,795 cases (donated by all sectors of society). The association actively prepares rickshaw puller insurance, which will be realized soon. Other tasks are also making rapid progress. In total, more than 20,000 members participate in various tasks every week.

Yang Meizhen Returns Home After Completing Her Studies 116

Ms. Yang Meizhen graduated from Shanghai University in 1930. She then served in the Chinese Women's Temperance Association as its deputy director. In the summer and autumn of 1934, she represented the Chinese Women's Temperance Association to attend the 17th World Women's Temperance Congress in Copenhagen, Denmark. To the esteemed director of the Shanghai Shenbao Newspaper:

Respectfully, upon reading your newspaper's local news section, it was reported that our company, at around 11:00 AM yesterday, suffered an accident in which a rickshaw puller was burned to death on the spot due to the negligence of a driver causing a gasoline explosion, and that gasoline was stored indoors. We hereby submit this letter to request a correction. There was no burning to death on the spot, and there was no gasoline stored indoors. All gasoline is dispensed at the American-style gasoline pump installed at our company's entrance. The incident involved a silversmith apprentice and two coppersmiths who were cooking together using a kerosene stove. Unexpectedly, the kerosene stove exploded, severely injuring one coppersmith and slightly injuring the other. They are currently residing at the Nanyang Hospital. The apprentice was not injured. We request a correction to this effect.

Respectfully, we wish you peace.

Reorganization of Shanghai Lawn Tennis Club into the Conly Athletic Club 141

Jointly Organized by the National Sports Federation and the Chinese Athletic Association

Membership Applications Now Open

The Shanghai Lawn Tennis Club on Conly Road is the only complete grass court in Shanghai. It was originally established by the National Sports Federation. Two years ago, due to the landlord reclaiming the land, Qiu Feihai continued to operate it. Due to poor management, it was forced to close last winter. However, it has been found that the exorbitant land tax requires a rent of around 2,000 yuan per year. With the addition of equipment and other expenses, even with the membership fees paid by the members, it was only enough to cover the expenses. Therefore, after Mr. Qiu's contract expired, no one was willing to take over. It would be a pity to let such a good venue go to waste. After discussions between the National Sports Federation and the Chinese Athletic Association on Hardoon Road, it was decided to jointly fund the club to maintain the grass tennis courts in Shanghai and to provide convenience for tennis enthusiasts. This will promote the development of tennis. The club has been renamed the Conly Athletic Club (Conly Athletic Club). It is now actively preparing, tidying up the grounds, building shelters, and repairing the surrounding bamboo fences. It will be completed soon, and membership applications are now open. The tennis courts will be open for play on April 10th. Those interested in joining can contact Mr. Li Baojun of Huadong Company at 583 Jing'an Temple Road. The club's regulations are listed below:

There are two types of membership: summer and winter. Apart from the winter regulations, which will be announced separately, the summer membership is divided into the following seven categories, with the quarterly fees set as follows: Special Member, 28 yuan; Ordinary Member, 36 yuan; Women's Member, 20 yuan; Student Member, 20 yuan; Foreign Member (regardless of gender), 50 yuan.

Members of the tennis department must pay fees according to the regulations. If a member withdraws midway, they are not entitled to a refund of the membership fee.

The summer season of the tennis department runs from April 10th to October 30th.

Members of the tennis department are entitled to the following rights: (A) The tennis department has several hard and grass courts at the old Shanghai Lawn Tennis Club site on Conly Road, and ball boys are provided. (B) The opening hours of the tennis department are as follows: Monday to Friday, 4:00 PM to 7:00 PM daily; Saturday, 2:00 PM to 7:00 PM; Sunday and public holidays, 7:00 AM to 11:00 AM and 2:00 PM to 7:00 PM. (C) The club may hold various tennis competitions from time to time to enhance the skills and interest of the tennis department members. (D) The club may select representatives to participate in various tennis competitions outside the club.

To avoid overcrowding on the tennis courts, members of the tennis department are requested to pay attention to the following points: (A) Members should not invite guests to play tennis at the club at will. (B) If a member needs to bring a guest to play tennis at the club, each person must pay one yuan for each session, but each guest is limited to one session per month. (C) Members must bring their membership card when they come to the club to play tennis. (D) Members must follow the membership sign-up schedule and take turns according to the sessions.

Membership Procedures: Students applying for membership must have a certificate from the school authorities. Anyone who wishes to join the club as a member must have one member of the club who is familiar with them (one proposer and one seconder) and must be reviewed according to the following regulations. All membership applications must be signed separately by the applicant, proposer, and seconder, and sent to the honorary secretary together with the membership fee and the tennis department fee. If the applicant is rejected by the club, the fees paid will be refunded in full.

Securities

Public Bond Deliveries in March Greatly Reduced

Yesterday, March 27th, was the settlement date for March

futures at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange. The small amount of deliveries

was unprecedented. The total amount was 4.44 million, of which 96 accounted for 3.055 million,

full length 45,000, and unified public bonds A and B totaled only 1.16 million. Most were

settlements for small retail investors. Since the reforms, all old bonds

have been suspended from trading on the market. Of the five types of unified public bonds, only A and B

had been exchanged before settlement. The other three types, C, D, and E, had not yet reached the exchange period, so they could not be traded as

March futures. Types A and B totaled 300 million, and

the actual amount delivered was only over 1 million. Moreover, since the financial sector experienced

the turmoil of the previous decision and major reforms, it has become wary, fearing that it would be easy to enter but difficult to exit, repeating

the previous pattern. The financial sector's wait-and-see attitude has also made it impossible for speculators

to get involved, and trading has sharply decreased. The exchange is increasingly deserted. Looking back on the past,

one cannot help but feel a sense of vicissitude. People's minds are scattered, and the market situation is declining. If there are no major changes in the environment

in April, it will not be easy to have hope for a thriving trade.

Since unified public bonds began trading as futures on February 28th,

excluding holidays, there have been only 24 trading days. In March, only types A and B

were traded. During these 24 days, the total number of transactions was only 3.85 million, which is rare.

Regarding the changes in market prices, on the first day of trading on February 28th,

after the previous turmoil, people's minds were extremely weak, and selling was extremely strong.

In one day, from morning to night, prices fell by about two yuan. After that, prices gradually recovered.

The highest price for type A was 66.5 yuan on March 9th, and the highest price for type B was 65.21 yuan on February 3rd. Compared to the lowest price

on February 28th, type A differed by 3.1 yuan, and type B differed by 3.7 yuan.

After this sharp drop and sudden rise, prices tended to fluctuate slightly, with minimal ups and downs, and trading was extremely

light. Although there were difficulties in Sino-Japanese negotiations, rumors of autonomy in Fujian Province, and disputes over the Rhine River

between Germany and France, the market seemed to be unaffected and had absolutely no hope.

The hopeless 96 public bonds, on the other hand, had a period of unjustified increase, from

9.2 yuan to 12.2 yuan, which shows that speculators felt that there was no way to go.

Since then, trading has become light, and most have turned to other exchanges. Therefore,

it will not be possible to reverse the fate of the securities market in the short term. The number of March futures deliveries

and clearings are listed below separately (unit: 100 yuan):
