Educational News 152

Within Liaoning Province

Progress of Enslavement Education:

The Future of National Thought is Lamentable

(Special dispatch from the Northeast News Agency, Shenyang) Currently, education in various parts of the Northeast has been completely Japanized. Among various courses, Japanese language and literature are the most emphasized, to the point where it seems one cannot have a meal without understanding Japanese. Northeastern youths, receiving this education, are increasingly developing a servile nature while their nationalistic thinking is diminishing daily. The future is truly deplorable. Here is a record of the Shenyang Japanese cultural promotion situation:

Pseudo-Fengtian Municipal Public Office Education

Shenyang Pro-Japanese Education: The Education Department of the Pseudo-Fengtian Municipal Public Office, in order to have teachers in municipal primary schools promote Japanese culture, selects pro-Japanese teachers to study in Japan every year. This year, even more effort will be put into Japanese culture by employing many excellent Japanese teachers and assigning them to various schools to establish a policy of enslavement education and anesthetic teaching methods.

Liaoyang Japanese Language School

In the year of Taisho 2 (1913), Liaoyang County hired Shigematsu Masui as a consultant for the Liaoyang Japanese Language School. He specifically established a night school in Yixue Hutong, south of the city, which has lasted for twenty-three years. According to the Japanese propaganda, if one knows Japanese, one can study all aspects of Japan. Moreover, now that "Manchukuo" and Japan are inseparable, graduates of the Japanese language school are achieving great success in all fields. The Japanese language school currently operated by the South Manchuria Railway is the predecessor of this night school. This year's graduates number over a hundred, and before graduation, suitable employment positions have already been secured. From this, one can deeply understand the Japanese method of winning over and anesthetizing young students.

This Year's Fujian Province

Education as the Central Task of Administration

(Dispatch from Fuzhou, 26th) Fujian Province has decided to make education the central task of administration this year. Chairman Chen has ordered commissioners and county heads in all districts that, henceforth, regarding education funding, the province will do its best to plan, and all districts and counties should strive to promote it. He also expressed intentions to improve the treatment of teacher union members and educational administrative personnel.

Hubei Province Compulsory Education

Report from the Ministry of Education's Special Commissioner, Zhen Sheng

The Ministry of Education issued an instruction to the Hubei Provincial Department of Education on the 26th, stating: "Based on the inspection report of Yang Zhensheng, the special commissioner hired by the Ministry for inspection, it has been found that the province's implementation of compulsory education still has areas that need improvement. Instructions are hereby given as follows:

There are many private schools in the province, enrolling over 200,000 children. Their influence is almost equal to that of primary schools in the province. In areas where there are no primary schools, their existence is indeed beneficial and can be tolerated. However, in areas implementing compulsory education, they actually hinder the promotion of new education. Efforts should be made to utilize and supervise their improvement. Those that are more complete should be converted into substitute primary schools. The department has a plan for training teachers in private schools, which was implemented in the previous year and is crucial. Efforts should be intensified to order all counties to focus on the training of teachers in private schools. During this year's summer vacation, those who can be trained should be included in the teacher training program as much as possible. Those that cannot be improved or do not accept training should be banned immediately, and the original students should be transferred to short-term primary schools or joint security primary schools. The number of public ordinary primary schools in the province is too small. In addition to encouraging private individuals to establish schools, joint security primary schools should be established according to the interim measures for establishing primary schools by joint security in the counties of the province. The schools should be converted into ordinary primary schools or simplified primary schools within ten years. The primary schools in cities such as Wuhan in the province are still insufficient to accommodate the majority of children, and the number of children out of school remains high. Expansion should be assisted and a two-shift system should be rigorously implemented to accommodate more students. Special education in the province is well-managed. Such educational measures should not be limited to recovered areas but should be promoted to a wider range. Adult classes should be opened in existing short-term primary schools and gradually expanded. The two hundred and forty short-term primary schools planned to be established have now all been established and should be reported for the record. The funding for short-term primary schools was discounted by 85% in the first half of the 24th year. It has been stated that starting from January of the 25th year, there will be no discounts, and the full amount is currently being issued. This should be reported for verification as soon as possible. The school buildings of most schools are simple and inadequate, and because they are old and in disrepair, they do not provide shelter from wind and rain. The department should establish a plan for renovating school buildings, prioritizing them according to urgency and renovating or repairing them annually, and not allow them to collapse or even pose a danger of collapse. All of the above should be complied with accordingly. This is an order from the Ministry of Education."

Jiangsu Province Normal School Student Examination

Regional Examinations to be Held Starting April 8th

Examination Locations for Each Region Have Been Determined

Notice Sent to County Bureaus to Submit Rosters

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education has stipulated that this year's graduation examination for students of normal schools and kindergarten normal departments will be held from April 8th to 11th, divided into regions. Notices have been sent to county bureaus for compliance. It has been learned that with the examination date approaching, the Department has designated the examination locations for each region as follows: First Region: Zhenjiang, examination location at Zhenjiang Normal School; Second Region: Wuxian, examination location at Suzhou Women's Normal School; Third Region: Rugao, examination location at Rugao Normal School; Fourth Region: Tongshan, examination location at Xuzhou Women's Normal School. The schools participating in the examination in each region this year have also been determined, and orders have been given to the county bureau chiefs of each region to compile and send a roster of examination students and transcripts of each subject, along with two 2-inch half-length photos of each student, to the Department within one week. Students participating in the examination will be notified in advance to arrive at the location of the examination to await the examination.

Guidelines for Cooperation Between Vocational Schools and Construction Organizations Defined by the Ministry of Education

The Ministry of Education has defined guidelines for cooperation between vocational schools and construction organizations, as reported yesterday. The guidelines are listed below: Vocational schools should agree with the internship organization on a detailed plan and work procedure for students' internships, and should strive to ensure that off-campus internships are closely related to the training received at school. Off-campus internships for vocational school students should be limited to senior students, and the internship time may be concentrated for convenience. During off-campus internships, the internship organization should designate personnel to provide guidance. If necessary, the school may provide a stipend, but the teacher who originally taught the internship course should be responsible for participating in the guidance to facilitate communication. If the cost of internship materials required for off-campus internships is too high, the school should bear part or all of the cost. At the end of the student's off-campus internship, the guiding personnel of the internship organization should summarize and evaluate the internship performance and grades of each student separately and submit them to the school for inclusion in the academic record.

Citywide Scout Fundraising Begins Yesterday

Fundraising for Clubhouse and Campsite Construction Aims for 50,000 Yuan Campsite Determined to be on Liuying Road

The City Scout Council, in order to plan for the completion of the construction of the Council's clubhouse and campsite, launched a fundraising campaign for construction funds by citywide scouts starting yesterday. The fundraising goal is set at 50,000 national currency. It is reported that the campsite has been determined to be on Liuying Road in Zhabei. A fundraising committee has been organized, with Mayor Wu serving as chairman and Tian Ding'an, Li Dachao, Li Qifan, Yu Kuiyuan, Shen Tong, Shen Siliang, Leng Xueqiao, Yao Shushu, Xu Peihuang, Xu Guozhi, Chen Heqin, Tong Xingbai, Zhao Weizu, Pan Gongzhan, Luo Lie, and others as members. Fundraising began yesterday. For all donations, whether from organizations or individuals, those donating 500 yuan or more will have their names inscribed at the clubhouse and campsite as a memento. Those donating 1,000 yuan or more will have their names inscribed at the clubhouse and campsite as a memento, and individuals will also have their photos displayed. Those donating 5,000 yuan or more will have a room named after them, and individuals will also have their photos displayed. Those donating 10,000 yuan or more will be reported by the Council to the China Scout General Association for commendation, and a hall will be named after them, with the individual's photo displayed. For those who donate land or other real estate, the value will be assessed and handled in accordance with the above methods. The donations will be announced in three phases. The first phase announcement will be on April 20th.

Jiang Dayi Lecture

The Cultural Era of the Wangbi Mountain Site (Part 1)

Mr. Jiang Dayi lectured at Cuiying Middle School in Suzhou the day before yesterday, entitled "The Era of the Wangbi Mountain Site Culture." The original text is as follows:

"Gentlemen, I am very honored to have the opportunity to gather with you all today. Originally, Mr. Jin Songcen and the principal of this school invited me to come here last Friday afternoon. However, things did not go as planned. On that afternoon, I had already arranged to meet several friends from Shanghai to investigate ancient sites on Tiger Hill. They all hold positions at the school, and Friday is not a holiday, but they specially took leave to come to Suzhou. Therefore, I had to accompany them, and had to postpone my time here until today. I am very sorry to all of you, and I must first sincerely apologize to you.

Mr. Jin Songcen and the principal of this school invited me to come here, but in reality, I am unlearned and have nothing to offer you. However, the two gentlemen's kindness should not be disappointed. Therefore, I forget my ignorance and am willing to present the issue of 'The Era of the Wangbi Mountain Site Culture' here for discussion with you all.

The location of the site: On November 24th of last year, Mr. Cao Huadan and I found a Wangbi Mountain cultural site located in the southwest outside of Suzhou City, about eight or nine li away from the city, near the town of Xinguo. The site is located on the northeast corner of Stone Lake, belonging to the 24th image of Yidu in the old Wu territory. A main road runs horizontally through the middle of the site, called Xingchun Bridge Street, which is the thoroughfare leading directly to Xinguo Town. Another main road surrounds the southwest of the site, which can lead to Lishu Town. Rivers surround the northwest of the site, which can lead to boats. On the south side of the site, there is a very poetic residence, which is the property of Mr. Yu Bingrenjue. According to Mr. Li Yinquan's research, this place should be the former site of Tianjing Pavilion in Fan Chengda's Stone Lake Villa of the Song Dynasty.

To the west of the site, there is a high bridge called Yuecheng Bridge, which is the Yuelaixi Bridge recorded in the Wu Junzhi. The river under the bridge, connected to the Stone Lake water, is the Hengtang River, which is the North Yuelaixi of the classics. To the west of Yuecheng Bridge, there is a long bridge lying on Stone Lake, which is our famous Xingchun Bridge in Suzhou. On the eighth month of the lunar calendar, everyone goes to Stone Lake to watch the moon, which is in this place. Crossing Xingchun Bridge, you have reached the west bank of Stone Lake. Along the bank are small mountains such as Mopan Mountain and Shangfang Mountain. These small mountains are all small peaks northeast of the Seven Sons Mountain. In ancient times, the Seven Sons Mountain was called Hengshan. These Mopan Mountain and Shangfang Mountain peaks did not have independent names at that time, and were collectively called Hengshan. (See Wang Wenke's Gusu Zhi for proof) Therefore, from the ancient place name, this site is east of Heng Mountain, if just the main peak, then one can say its at the northeast side of the foot of the Heng Mountain.

School Survey Shanghai American School Overview (4) Hu Zuyin 153

Three Language:

Can clearly and powerfully express opinions.

Can write short articles, indicating the ability to use sentences and clauses.

Understands and can write ordinary commercial letters.

Can take notes and can explain or write articles based on the outline.

Recognizes subjects and verbs in sentences.

Understands the eight major parts of speech in grammar.

Can memorize at least five poems in a year.

Four Writing:

Can write at least sixty characters per minute.

Can submit clear and clean course papers for each subject.

Five Arithmetic:

Can achieve 80% accuracy in calculating the four operations.

Can calculate ordinary fractions.

Can read and write four-digit decimals.

Can do addition, subtraction, multiplication, and division problems with decimals.

Understands and can apply the tables of length, weight, water volume, dry volume, time, and area.

Can do addition, subtraction, multiplication, and division problems with fractions.

Understands the meaning of percentages and can find the percentages of each number.

Understands banks and banking.

Understands the concept of simple interest and can calculate interest using ordinary methods.

Can answer the practice problems in the practice book.

The school's disciplinary and pastoral measures can be divided into two aspects: positive and negative. On the positive side, the school emphasizes the influence of teachers' personality and indirect suggestion. According to the school principal's opinion, although the school's teachers have the dignity of teachers, they have never used this dignity to oppress or subdue students. The school's teachers often use the method of personality influence to enhance the friendly relationship between teachers and students, so that students can have automatic awareness in the melting of the teachers' personality, and can automatically improve their behavior. The so-called indirect suggestion refers to promoting the improvement of student behavior through environmental pressure and group sanctions. For example, a newly admitted student is not clean in terms of body and clothing; the school authorities do not immediately train this student to be clean in body and clothing. However, after the student joins the school environment, he will unconsciously feel that his unclean body and clothes cannot adapt to this clean environment, so he will automatically improve. If he is in this environment and still has no automatic feeling, then other students will give him an indication, or even notify him that he must have some improvement; otherwise, the group will despise him or reject him. Therefore, he is in this good group life, under the pressure of the environment and the sanctions of the group, he must correct his personal behavior to adapt to the environment.

As for the negative disciplinary measures, the school usually uses the method of demerits. For example, if a student is late several times, he will be given several small demerits. After accumulating a certain number of small demerits, certain rights will be deprived; this deprivation of rights will not hinder his physical and mental health and academic work. If he can correct his mistakes, the deprived rights can be restored, so that he can have the opportunity to reform himself. If a student commits a serious mistake, the principal will study the problem child in detail and give appropriate solutions or punishments. When necessary, the principal can use corporal punishment, suspension, expulsion, and other severe punishments to deal with stubborn students. However, according to the school principal's report, these severe punishment methods are rarely used.

Commercial News

The Financial Situation Over the Past Year (6) 154

— He Boxiong

Upon examination, the government's announced equalization taxes over the past year can be divided into two periods. The first is before the promulgation of the new currency law on November 3rd of last year, and the second is after the promulgation of the new currency law on November 3rd. Before the promulgation of the new currency law, the equalization tax was not levied according to established rules. After it came into effect on November 4th, the equalization tax announced by the government was not only no less than the theoretically expected equalization tax, but often exceeded it. Consider the table below: (Note 10)

Therefore, before November 10th, there was still a significant profit to be made from shipping silver from Shanghai to London. The net profit from exporting every hundred yuan, after deducting freight, could range from about twenty-six yuan to about forty-one yuan. The government did not completely restrict the export of silver through equalization taxes. As a result, as of the end of January of the 24th year of the Republic (1935), the silver reserves of Shanghai banks only totaled 335 million yuan, a decrease of over 225 million yuan compared to the same period last year. Compared to the highest point in the 22nd year (1933), the decrease was nearly 300 million yuan. At the end of February, there was a further decrease of over 2.1 million yuan compared to the previous month, and at the end of March, there was another decrease of over 9 million yuan compared to the end of February. In April and May, there were slight increases, while in June, the reserves were slightly low, mainly because it was the peak season for wheat sales in the interior, and also because it was approaching the Dragon Boat Festival, and money was extremely tight in various places, requiring cash. Therefore, in that month, silver dollars were slightly transferred to the interior. In July and August, because the autumn harvest of inland products was approaching, the need for cash was particularly urgent, and 4 to 5 million yuan was transferred out in the two months, with 2.4 million yuan sent to Hankou, and about 500,000 yuan each to Beijing, Tianjin, and other places. From September to November, there were cash inflows, mainly because Shanghai's financial situation was becoming more stable, exchange rates were narrowing, and foreign silver prices were not rising as sharply as before. Therefore, the cash previously shipped for export was gradually being returned. However, the percentage of total reserves held by Chinese banks was still much higher than that of foreign banks. Shen Bao Women's Special

Japanese Women's Views on Occupations 155

— Yifa

Japanese women, produced under the educational method of "good wives and wise mothers," naturally have their own characteristics. They have only reached occupational equality with men and have not yet taken the step of participating in politics. In the past, Japanese women only engaged in lower-level occupations such as maids and geishas. Recently, the scope of women's occupations has expanded considerably, and there is a possibility of reaching the same level as men in terms of income. Particularly among primary school teachers, women have already begun to replace men. However, in general occupations, they are still working under the guidance of men. In terms of occupational status, they may even be inferior to women in our country.

Women in rural areas can also work in the fields in the same way as men, and in addition to cooking and preparing meals, they also have to collect firewood and raise children. In reality, they are more hardworking than men. Women in coastal areas can spend all day naked underwater, catching fish and shellfish, called "ama" (sea women). Their endurance and diligence are superior even to men. As the wheel of time turns, young women in rural areas desperately go to the cities, leading to the emergence of many new occupations.

Waitresses in cafes and hotels occupy a very important position in Japanese women's occupations. They greet people with smiles all day long and pour wine for customers. Due to the environment, excellent women are often plunged into the abyss. Although this type of occupation is also despised, the development of cafes and pubs is still increasing day by day. Large cafes and pubs in Ginza often employ two or three hundred waitresses. Smaller ones usually have notices posted year-round, recruiting waitresses. Therefore, it is very easy for young and beautiful women to become cafe waitresses when they are unemployed, which is a special phenomenon in Japanese women's occupations.

Public canteens and department stores are now entirely staffed by women. Male staff members stand on the sidelines and are overshadowed. They are very capable of winning the praise of customers and are loyal to their duties. They are more attentive and courteous than men. Customers and male staff members can also respect each other, so there are few instances of lewdness or jesting, which is commendable.

Women have also been employed in all positions on public buses and some positions as ticket sellers on trams. They are familiar with complicated matters, can explain the names of stops, and help the elderly and children. Therefore, grateful people often anonymously give gifts to female ticket sellers, which is a beautiful story. Other ticket sales positions in theaters and movie theaters are almost all filled by women. Therefore, Japanese women have taken over all ticket selling positions, except for the few women employed as ticket sellers at train stations.

Employing maids and the system of keeping servants are still prevalent in Japan. Maids manage cleaning, tidying, cooking, and laundry. Servants are often used to look after children, and the treatment is similar to that in our country. Only middle-class families or above can afford to employ them. Most ordinary shops in Japan are family-run side businesses, so housewives often manage the shop in addition to household chores. Therefore, shops can reduce employee expenses and are easier to maintain. Although their level of education is above secondary school, they are not ashamed of managing small shops or working as clerks, which is completely different from most newly educated women in our country.

Although there are also female staff members in banks and public organizations, their positions are not high, and they only work as receptionists and guides. Therefore, the occupation of Japanese women is either under the control of men or involves serving others.

Women and Children's Music Education 156

— Shamei

The reason why the academic music movement in China has not achieved widespread development naturally has objective and subjective reasons. However, from the perspective of the music movement itself, the main reason, in addition to being influenced by the entire Chinese culture, is the consistent neglect of children's music movement, that is, the so-called basic policy of music.

If children's music is highly developed, it will produce a large number of musician cells, or at least create seeds for many pure music appreciators. These are all predictable facts.

The path of children's music movement is children's music education. That is to say, if children's music education is developed, then children's musical knowledge will be widespread, and as a result, children's musical activities will be easily expanded.

Women are consistently close to children, so in principle and in fact, women should assume special tasks for the development of children's music education. At the very least, they cannot shirk their responsibility for enlightening music education.

At the same time, women seem to be naturally rich in musical emotions. Although when the world's musicians are tallied up, women account for a very small number, this does not prove that women's musical abilities are particularly lower than men's, but because women are hindered by their children and families, they cannot consistently pursue musical cultivation, and they often simply stop their efforts after marriage. However, it is most appropriate to use the musical knowledge that women have already acquired for children's music education, and children can easily accept it.

Women naturally have a kind of soft attitude towards children, and this attitude is exactly what is needed for children's music education. In Europe, especially in the United States, most of the elementary school music teachers are women, which shows that women are very suitable for this career. For example, after a child is born, the first thing they hear is their mother's lullaby.

Examining the great musicians, their preliminary musical cultivation almost always comes from their mothers.

Children's Diseases Due to Malnutrition 157

— Yuxiu

Children's nutritional problems are the most difficult to deal with. For mothers, arranging their children's food is a very difficult task. It is common to see children with yellowish complexions and thin bodies, crying incessantly, making mothers unable to rest day or night. This is a common phenomenon of children getting sick due to malnutrition. Specifically, diseases such as emaciation, rickets, beriberi, and scurvy are all caused by malnutrition. Now, I will briefly explain the symptoms of these diseases and the dietary precautions to be taken in ordinary times for the reference of mothers. If the disease is more serious, it is still necessary to seek medical treatment.

Rickets

There are many causes, the most important of which are: 1. Pregnant women who are still breastfeeding do not have enough calcium in their bodies; 2. Lack of vitamin D in food; 3. Lack of fat and unhealthy living habits.

The symptoms of this disease mostly occur during the teething period of children (minor cases are not easily noticed). Such as slight fever, irritability, restless sleep, those who can walk have a weak gait and do not like to walk, severe cases have very obvious muscle symptoms, or even paralysis, the anterior and posterior fontanelles do not close, the teeth are small and strange, the bone ends become large, the skin is pale, etc.

Scurvy

The cause is lack of vitamin C in food. People who live on ships and cannot get fresh food often have this disease.

Symptoms include weight loss, weakness, pale complexion, spongy gums that bleed easily, bad breath, heart palpitations, headaches, etc. In severe cases in children, the bones separate from the bone shafts.

Beriberi

The cause is lack of vitamin B in food. It is easy to get this disease from eating machine-made white rice.

Infants with this disease can die in a few hours (symptoms similar to the latter). Older children may experience heart palpitations, edema (sometimes none), paralysis, weak limbs, abdominal discomfort, pale complexion, paralyzed limbs, sometimes loss of appetite, nausea, vomiting, etc. Symptoms.

Nutritional Attention

Speaking of nutritional problems, fresh milk is naturally the best food because it contains the most vitamins, but it is too expensive, which poses an economic problem, and it is not easy to buy in many places. Soy milk can usually be used as a substitute, and two to three pounds should be consumed daily. Eggs and liver (pork liver, beef liver) should be eaten often because they also contain many vitamins. Vegetables, various vegetables such as green vegetables, cabbage, mustard greens, spinach, all contain vitamins A, B, C, and D. Children who can eat them should eat more, and breastfeeding mothers can cook them in soups or make them into vegetable purees. Fruits such as oranges, grapes, lemons, tangerines, tomatoes (tomatoes contain the same substances as tangerines, but are cheaper), grapes, etc. contain vitamins B and C. Fruits taste good and are appetite stimulants. It is not advisable to use completely white rice. It is advisable to use brown rice and eat pasta foods often to prevent beriberi. Beans should also be eaten often, which can not only prevent beriberi but also contain many carbohydrates, which can lead to obesity. Give fresh beef juice or broth, potato soup, and orange juice as an important food to prevent blood diseases. Infants five or six months old should add orange juice to their milk. The best diet for rickets is breast milk. When infants are breastfed, barley soup, rice water, etc. can be added.

All kinds of food should be cooked soft, easy to digest, and not fried.

Standard Woman

The White House Hostess as a Political Activist 158

— Yingdai

-- Shrewdness and decisiveness that men cannot match --

Since Mrs. Roosevelt moved into the White House, she has traveled 40,000 miles, given 92 speeches, received 100,050 letters, and given radio speeches for the American Mutual Aid Association, earning $36,000 in American dollars. These records are enough to show how active she is. Moreover, since becoming the hostess of the White House, she has guided all the housework in a large family. Every First Lady is like this. After entering the White House, all charitable organizations will come to donate money, and she will naturally donate some according to the Roosevelt family's charitable nature.

Anyone who is close to her knows that she will not lose any energy and optimism, even though she is so busy with various activities and speeches in two years. In the coming year, she has already planned what work should be done each week in the previous year, but long-distance travel cannot be planned beforehand.

Was it the year before last? She had been to Puerto Rico and the Virgin Islands to investigate charitable causes. Last year, she was already preparing to go to Honolulu and spend the summer in the forest, but in the end, she was too busy to go.

Mrs. Roosevelt's flight to Puerto Rico was not the furthest trip on the 1934 travel chart, because she also went to the Virgin Islands, which are 6,632.8 miles away. The journey by small boat to the islands after getting off the plane was not included.

When she went to the Pacific coast to greet President Roosevelt when he returned from Honolulu in the summer of the year before last, her journey was 10,978 miles. At the end of June, she left Washington in a new sports car, the first new car she bought after moving into the White House.

On the journey, she traveled 2,000 miles, passing through West Virginia, Tennessee, and Kentucky. On July 8, she arrived in Chicago. On the way, she went to the countryside in West Virginia and Tennessee to conduct field investigations into social problems.

From Chicago to Sagamore, she traveled by plane, a total of 1,919 miles. By this time, her traveling life had been going on for a month. California newspapers said that she was at Lake Tahoe because her beloved daughter, Mrs. Dahl, was going through a divorce at that time.

Later, she spent a week at Lake Tahoe and Yosemite Valley. Finally, she rushed to the Pacific to meet Roosevelt. Then, she and the President and his entourage went to various places to conduct investigations. In short, her 40,000-mile journey was counted very accurately by those close to her.

The letters received by Mrs. Roosevelt were constantly sent to the White House every day, and there was indeed no interruption in the two years. However, she did not read most of these letters. Questions about political issues were handed over to the government for reply, and other letters were replied to by her secretary.

However, there were many letters that she opened herself. These letters were probably to provide help in economic and emotional matters. If possible, these letters were answered satisfactorily. However, letters asking for private donations were also handled by the secretary, because there were sometimes about 300 of these letters a week.

The 92 speeches mentioned above by Mrs. Roosevelt, like her travels, are recorded very reliably. She only says less, not more, because she will give a speech whenever a problem arises. The short and unnoticed ones are not included. The ninety times mentioned here are only formal speeches and radio broadcasts.

In the summer of 1934, she gave a radio speech for the Mutual Aid Association and earned $3,000 per speech. However, she later donated this huge amount of money entirely to charitable organizations.

Special Report

A Visit to Ms. Zhang Lizhen, President of the Shanghai YWCA 159

— Jiping

After Mrs. Jin Longzhang, president of the Shanghai YWCA, went to Yunnan, the association's affairs were presided over by Ms. Zhang Lizhen. Everyone finds this Ms. Zhang's name very unfamiliar, so they only know her as Mrs. He Linyi. When we mention Zhang Lizhen, we must first talk about her father - Zhang Chanfen. Mr. Zhang has served the Commercial Press for many years. He is a truly remarkable person, who is always eager to help others and enthusiastic about education. He not only cultivated his own children to be successful, but also founded many schools to educate other people's children. Readers all know that there are two schools with a long history in Shanghai, one is Qingxin Middle School and the other is Qingxin Girls' Middle School. The principals of the two schools, Zhang Shilin and Zhang Rongzhen, are Mr. Zhang's sons and daughters. They are a family of educators, and they are indeed worthy of admiration.

A Life of Music

Although this Ms. Lizhen is not a principal, she has been consistently diligent in serving the cause of social education. People say that she is a leader in the women's movement and a new good wife and wise mother. She herself once said: "Some of my father's work ethic has been passed on to me!" This shows the greatness of the influence of family education. She especially loves music and has had a bit of talent since she was a child. After graduating from McTyeire School, she stayed at her alma mater as a music teacher. In 1916, she studied at the Oberlin Conservatory of Music in the United States, worked hard, and achieved great success. She recalled her time in the United States, saying: "Some of our classmates had already turned gray, but they were still very interested and had a more vigorous spirit than women in our country. I felt that I used my parents' hard-earned money, so I didn't dare to slack off. I also thought that the opportunity to study in the United States in my lifetime might only be these two years, so I stepped up my efforts and lived much more difficult lives than government-funded students. … For the past twenty years, I have still lived a life of music. First, I served as a music instructor at Tsinghua University in Beiping. In recent years, I have been a music instructor at Moore Memorial Girls' School for four and a half days a week in Shanghai. Music is my only hobby. There is always a concert at sea. I am either performing" or appreciating it. Some people have advised me to retire and stop working, but I think that I can't bear to give up more than twenty years of hard work once. I hope this ambition will not wane as I get old!"

Street Children Have a Way to Live

I asked her which social cause she is currently involved in that she finds the most interesting. She said: "Although I am a director of Qingxin Girls' Middle School, Pu Yi Xiang, and the YWCA, I have made no contribution. Only the Fu Tong Suo (Orphanage) has been more meaningful. I didn't feel that there were too many refugees when I was in Beiping. When I arrived in Shanghai, I found many miserable street children everywhere. I thought about ways to help them. Three years ago, I co-founded the 'Fu Tong Suo' with Mr. Li Zhengahui and others. Last year, we moved to a new site in Jiangwan, providing education and handicrafts to orphaned street children so that they can have a skill to support themselves. It is also a solution to social problems. One end. However, at the beginning of the establishment, the economy was not very prosperous. I hope that enthusiastic people will do their best to help. I think that although street children are in a difficult situation, those who are talented and self-motivated may have more hope than the children of wealthy families.

Women Must Be Self-Aware

I also asked her what she thinks of working women today. She said, "There are currently four phenomena in the job market: Everyone is looking for a job but can't find the right one; everything is asking for people but can't find the right person; once they have a job, they are unwilling to be truly responsible; they protect their own position and don't care about other people's suffering. These four situations are the same for men and women in today's society. So, women's careers can't be developed for the time being." I said, then what does Mrs. He hope for women? "This is hard to say. I mean, women who only eat and don't care about things should use their brains to do some good deeds: working women should have perseverance, be responsible, and not be extravagant; those who have been cultivated by the public should try their best to seek public welfare; ladies with good family conditions should generously donate to public welfare, and embody the virtue of heaven's love for life, and not be just grandchildren and cattle and horses, this is the supreme virtue of helping others and helping yourself! ..."

Women Under Fascism 160

— Meng Su

-- Depriving women of their rights and promoting national power --

In the modern women's liberation movement, being devastated by fascism is enough to make the spring peaches and plums lose their color.

Fascism is an overbearing military rule, which fundamentally opposes so-called civil rights and women's liberation. It advocates that everything be manipulated by a dictator supported by a group of warriors. Women are just appendages under male warriors; they are only fit to nurture future warriors and to serve veterans.

Mussolini once said bluntly: The vocation of women is to obey. Women's participation in politics will weaken the power of the country. Do you know why Anglo-Saxons are gradually coming to an end? It is because women's rights have expanded! In our country, there is absolutely no talk of women's participation in politics.

In fascist countries, all elections are manipulated by the leaders. Women's fascist groups must be subordinate to men's organizations. Female party members must be at least twenty-two years old to be eligible. In politics, they cannot stand on their own and can only follow behind male party members and listen to their instructions.

University education in Italy was originally non-gender-specific. Some middle-aged and older female professors were also quite well-known. However, after the fascists came to power, they formulated new regulations: male students over the age of eleven must not be taught by female teachers in subjects related to character development.

Women cannot be warriors, so women are just reproductive tools for warriors. Encouraging childbirth and increasing the population is one of Italy's domestic policies. The minimum marriage age in Italy was originally set at fifteen for women and eighteen for men. Now it has been reduced to fourteen for women and sixteen for men. This is tantamount to using the law to destroy women and put them on the road to premature aging.

In the past, the laws of some countries allowed men to whip their wives, as long as the whip was no thicker than the thumb, it was considered innocent. Now, no country has such an unequal law. The new Italian criminal law is particularly lenient in punishing men who abuse their wives or children. If a man inflicts injury or illness on his wife due to his own negligence, he used to be sentenced to imprisonment for up to five years; now he is only sentenced to detention for up to six months. Those who abuse their wives to death were formerly charged with violent homicide; now they have been reduced to imprisonment for up to eight years. In this way, husbands have the freedom to whip their wives, and as long as they are not beaten to the point of breaking bones, the victims have no recourse.

Also, if a wife runs away from her husband's home because she cannot stand her husband's abuse, she can be reported to the police and punished with imprisonment for up to one year or a fine of more than 1,000 to 10,000 lira. As for husbands who leave home because they are not satisfied with their wives, they are not subject to legal sanctions.

Italy's current criminal law ... wives who commit adultery are sentenced to imprisonment for up to two years. This is unique in European countries today. However, married men who commit adultery are not prohibited by law. Old law: Men who discover their wives, daughters, or biological sisters committing adultery and kill them are sentenced to imprisonment for three to seven years. Now, the fascist new law gives special leniency to men who kill their wives, daughters, or biological sisters for reasons of honor.

The punishment for women who lose their chastity is so severe, while the punishment for men who commit adultery is so light. To what extent does this deformed law degrade the status of women!

China has a man-eating code of ethics, and foreign countries have man-eating laws. When will women's layers of shackles be liberated?

A Sketch of Life in a Girls' School 161

— Qi Feng

It's a bitterly cold winter morning.

The morning bell has rung, but the students in the dormitory haven't gotten up yet. They're still dreaming rosy dreams in their warm, cozy blankets!

Winter is indeed cold, with northwest winds sharp as knives blowing against people; it's so unbearably cold! No wonder the students want to stay in bed!

"Huh? Where did my socks go?" The big, snow-like figure in the mosquito net asks herself.

"What time is it?" Hui asks, yawning in her blanket.

"Oh! The morning bell has already rung; it's almost time for breakfast!" Fen peeks her head out and says, looking at her watch.

"Get up, get up!" Old lady Qian calls from her bed.

A flurry of activity, as a group of young ladies emerges from their beds, still yawning and stretching.

As they exclaim sweetly, "Ah! Ah!"

"Dong! Dong! Dong!" The second bell rings, signaling breakfast time.

And so, a group of young ladies lines up and heads to the dining hall.

Heads form a chain, winding and curving into the dining hall door; instantly, the dining hall is lively with people!

After a period of chaos, the dining hall is silent, with only the sounds of chopsticks and bowls touching.

After a while, there's another flurry of activity as the young ladies head back to the dormitory to wash up!

Special Feature

A Brief History of Women's Affairs in Shanghai, China () 162

— Yang Chen Beiru

Everyone knows that promoting education for both the emperor and the common people is an urgent task for revitalizing China. It is hoped that in the future, with the help of all sectors, these schools will flourish and thrive, and that their students will be nurtured by the gentle breeze and timely rain, which will benefit not only this association. Recalling the January 28th Incident, we exerted our utmost efforts to care for wounded soldiers, donate supplies, and protect civilians. We also contributed to aviation donations, doing our best to fulfill our national duty. Furthermore, we enthusiastically supported various charitable organizations such as schools for the blind, orphanages, women and children's hospitals, Jiangwan children's teaching centers, and women's temperance societies, and were happy to see their success. My colleagues consider Shanghai to be the largest market in the Far East, with officials and dignitaries from all over the world coming and going. Whenever important foreign groups or dignitaries come to China for visits, the association sincerely guides them to visit scenic spots and present the spirit of our country, so that they can develop a good impression of our country. The reception of the American Economic Survey Mission, the Austrian Women's Righteousness Group, and the Los Angeles Chamber of Commerce Women's Group are particularly noteworthy examples. Educating Criminals 172

— Jia Wei

According to Company A: The warden of the Second Jiangsu Prison in this city believes that educating criminals is highly valued in civilized countries. Therefore, he has specifically written to the Chinese Buddhist Association, requesting that it appoint a Dharma master to come to the prison to give Buddhist lectures, so that they can reach the other shore together. It is heard that the Chinese Buddhist Association believes that the number of prisoners in the prison is the highest in the country, and that it is important to promote Buddhism and influence their psychology. It has been decided to appoint Zhong Kanghou to take charge of this matter and to gather Dharma masters and lay practitioners to give lectures at any time.

Regarding life in prison, with such a long period of time without freedom, how do the prisoners get by? This is something that we "free people" on the outside cannot know. However, by reading the newspaper, we can occasionally learn some snippets of their lives. For example, in a certain prison in a certain place, prisoners rebelled by going on a "hunger strike" because they couldn't stand the kind of life they were living inside. In a certain prison at a certain time, "disturbances" were caused by the prisoners due to insufficient food. In addition, there is also the case of old prisoners taking advantage of new prisoners and causing a violent fight, and even death row inmates being prayed for and confessing by religious priests at the execution ground in preparation for entering "heaven"... All of these are condensed forms of the lives that prisoners live, right?

As for what kind of educational work is carried out in prisons, apart from the so-called "model prisons" and the unique "reformatories," I have not heard of any. Now, the Second Prison in this city is indeed "valuing" the "educational work" of prisoners, which cannot but be a welcome thing!

Originally, crime has become one of the serious social maladies of today. Along with social poverty and class disparity, the number of crimes is bound to increase day by day. As far as criminology is concerned, crimes are divided into two types: "objective" and "subjective." Criminals are also divided into three types: "instinctive" (innate) criminals, "habitual" criminals (which are further divided into "professional" and "accidental habitual criminals"), and "occasional" criminals.

Speaking of civilized countries valuing the education of criminals, as far as we know, most of the treatment methods are divided into two types: "separate confinement system" and "graded system." The former aims to cut off the opportunity for prisoners to learn evil from each other; the latter treats first-time offenders with a relatively harsh life as the first level, followed by joint work, and finally a free level...

However, in today's Second Prison in this city, the authorities are "valuing" the education of criminals by starting with "propagating Buddhism," which cannot but be disappointing. Religion—Buddhism, in today's world, is indeed being "valued" and utilized in this way. The famous "Kalachakra Initiation Ceremony" and "Disaster Relief Conference" are all their masterpieces. Therefore, due to their "purpose" and their "great aspirations," the result of the so-called "Dharma masters and lay practitioners" "propagating Buddhism" and "influencing the psychology" of prisoners is predictable!

Originally, no one would deny that the main causes of general crime and the increase in the number of crimes are inextricably linked to the objective environment of society. A certain sociologist said based on his research: "The number of thefts and the rise in the price of bread maintain a constant positive correlation"! Isn't that so? A pickpocket who came out of prison after only a week finally resumed his old "three hands" business and was locked up again because he couldn't find a job and couldn't get food. This was only a few days ago.

Therefore, if we want to "educate criminals" and "influence their psychology," we should first "face" the fundamental problems of reality! All the nice-sounding empty words and methods will not last!

The Magic Lantern Show 174

— Shi Feng

This spring is a "false spring." It's almost the sixth day of March, but we still can't take off our cotton clothes. The wind sneaks sharply into our sleeves like a slick rat, making us feel like it's crawling all over us. As dusk approaches, the sky becomes even more desolate, and the streets become somewhat deserted. The entire small town is trapped in a terrifying situation. Rows of houses and trees are all sobbing silently.

Jin Jizhi, as if without any strength, breathed a sigh, put down his carrying pole, looked around, and sighed again.

What to do? It's getting dark soon, where should he go?

He walked out of a dilapidated temple in the morning and wandered through the streets and alleys, hoping that something would lead him forward. A group of children followed him like a monkey on a leash. Finally, he found a place, set up his frame, and tapped the small copper gong. A group of students dressed as children crowded around. He used the drumstick to draw a circle in front of the crowd, then pointed to the pictures and said in a hoarse voice:

—Look inside: there's Zhang Zuolin fighting Wu Peifu, the 19th Route Army fighting the Japanese, ... and Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek leading the Northern Expedition...

As he spoke, he looked around to see if there was anyone who might object. He dropped the first few pictures, revealing half of a picture of several naked women:

—Ah, this one is called "Picking Grapes," it's a bit racy. Look at this child... there's also a young woman, and an old mother...

He dropped this picture and another new one appeared: it was carved out of wood, two people who looked like an old couple hugging each other. When he pulled and released the string, the two people kissed each other intimately. The children laughed loudly. So he happily tapped the picture with the drumstick and said with excitement:

—This is nothing special, the special part is inside. When you pull this string, there are fun things to see inside!... Who wants to watch? Who wants to watch?...

He tapped the drumstick on each glass window, staring straight ahead, hoping that all five viewing spots would be filled immediately, and then he could start the second round. However, after waiting for two or three minutes, only two children sat down to watch, with three spots still empty. He couldn't start it like this. So he had to take matters into his own hands and pull the potential customers, because according to his past experience, many people wanted to watch but were too embarrassed. Especially here on the street, so close to their homes, if their fathers or older brothers saw them watching, it would be awkward. But as long as he pulled them with his hand, they would sit down. He pulled two young men nearby and said: —Hey brother, do me a favor... help me out. The good stuff is inside. It's cold standing here, sit down and watch, sit down and watch...

The two men looked at each other, smiled, and sat down. He couldn't wait any longer, so he sang a little tune and pulled down the pictures one by one. The children exclaimed loudly at the scenes of war inside, and the young men hoped that he would quickly pull down the second picture, the third picture,... and get to the last two pictures soon. They were no longer paying attention to the war scenes. He thought to himself: faster, faster. At this moment, two young girls of fifteen or sixteen years old came and sat down, sharing one viewing spot. ... This is terrible, really, there's no way to continue the show: how can he show those pictures with girls watching?... But the two young men were even more interested and urged him to continue. Past "Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek leading the Northern Expedition" was "The Vineyard," what to do? He had no choice but to beg the girls to leave, but they were so stubborn and insisted on watching!

Go on, let them watch! Just don't blush!

The young men snickered. The girls watched intently without saying a word. So he continued the show.... When it was about to change to the next picture, he was very worried, but he was urged on, so he had to clap the board with the bell, and the picture inside changed. With this change, the two young men laughed loudly, the children also made a fuss, but the girls angrily cursed and left! He had to smile bitterly, apologize, and continue to play!

One after another, he earned some money. He ate a slightly more filling meal in the morning. But in the afternoon, no matter where he went, no one watched. Many children shouted and jumped as they went home to ask for money, but they never came back the same way they went: some pouting, some even shedding tears.

It was getting dark. Where to go? He sighed, watched the dusk gradually deepen, and walked towards the temple where he had stayed last night!

Story Beneath Mount Ma'an 175

— Yan

"Brother Tao San has been arrested!" Little Pockmark, who was working in the fields with Brother Tao San, ran back to tell Sister-in-law Tao San.

The sun was right overhead, and Sister-in-law Tao San was carrying a lunch basket, preparing to go to the fields when she ran into Little Pockmark's report on the bank of the field. This report was like a sharp arrow, piercing through Sister-in-law Tao San's heart, and she fell to the ground on the bank. Immediately, people from the surrounding area gathered around. By the time Sister-in-law Tao San woke up, almost everyone under Mount Ma'an was here. Everyone was arguing and guessing the reason for Brother Tao San's arrest.

"Alright, she's awake." Old Man Tang pushed through the crowd as if mediating a dispute and approached Sister-in-law Tao San. He was the elder under Mount Ma'an. Although they didn't have the titles of village chief or town chief, Old Man Tang's words still carried some weight. He sat on the ground and pushed Little Pockmark, saying, "Tell me exactly what happened? Speak slowly."

Little Pockmark was the public servant of the families under Mount Ma'an. During the busy farming season, he helped with work in turns. His reward was a full stomach and a place to sleep. He had plenty of strength, and he had patted his chest and said: Twenty or thirty people are really nothing to me! But he felt that today's events were too unexpected. He stared at Sister-in-law Tao San's pale face and stammered:

"Today Brother Tao San was happy, and we were dividing the field bank to work. At first, there were only two passersby who greeted Brother Tao San, but they didn't say many words before they started fighting... and they just grabbed him and took him away..."

Little Pockmark's face turned red, as if he were struggling to create a story. Little Pockmark usually liked to exaggerate when telling stories, and some of the men laughed when they saw him. But Old Man Tang hit Little Pockmark's calf with his dry tobacco pipe, saying:

"Where did your legs go? Don't lie, tell me clearly so we can deal with it!"

Seeing Old Man Tang's tense face, Little Pockmark seemed even more flustered. But as he hesitated, Old Man Tang's dry tobacco pipe made a second demonstration on his calf. Although he could clench his teeth and endure a few blows from even the heaviest stick, he was afraid of that tense face, and finally shouted out in a panic like a child:

"I just pulled down my pants to take a shit!"

The people around burst into thunderous laughter, and a look of sorrowful tears appeared on Sister-in-law Tao San's pale face. Old Man Tang hit Little Pockmark's buttocks with his dry tobacco pipe again, asked his wife to help Sister-in-law Tao San into the house, confidently instructed everyone to go back to work, and followed Sister-in-law Tao San into her house.

Sister-in-law Tao San had no appetite to eat, and Old Man Tang helped her clean up. Then he watched Old Man Tang pace back and forth in the house. Not even the time it takes to burn an incense stick had passed when the local constable A Xing sneaked in like a thief. When he saw Old Man Tang, he was stunned, but Old Man Tang shouted at him: "A Xing, you've done a good deed!"

"I'm just here to report the news," A Xing smiled flatteringly, "Landlord Zhang just sent someone to arrest Brother Tao San, saying that Brother Tao San still owes five dou of old rent..."

Old Man Tang repeatedly tapped the ground with his dry tobacco pipe, as if the ground were his enemy, "I, Old Man Tang, also owe him rent, why didn't you arrest me? Hmph, you've done a good deed! My wife is old, not as pretty as Sister-in-law Tao San!"

Old Man Tang spoke with urgency, standing like a door god in front of A Xing, shooting fire-like glances at him, and putting his dry tobacco pipe against his neck, saying:

"A Xing, how much money did you take from Landlord Zhang? You eat the food of Mount Ma'an, you can't marry Sister-in-law Tao San as your wife, so you came up with this vicious plan. I, Old Man Tang, am willing to risk my old age to see if you still have food to eat under Mount Ma'an!" (To be continued)

Don Patricio

Nonsense 177

Hitler recently gave a speech in Jena, saying that the Treaty of Versailles should be a tombstone, only enough for people to hang and mourn in front of. Tan Lao San said that although the old tombstones are lying in the weeds and trampled by shepherds and woodcutters, there are still many new tombstones being erected, one by one, which can still make archaeologists weep and kneel and kowtow. Alas.

The truth about the box corpse case at the Beijing East Railway Station a few days ago has been revealed. The reason was due to a love triangle between master and servant. Tan Lao San said that the ancients said that lust is the root of all evil. From this case, we can see that the words of the ancients are not wrong after all.

Silver Jottings 183

— Zhi Er

Mr. Wu Cun's best "self-criticism" is these two famous words: "Love makes one want them to live, hating makes one want them to die." "(The likes of Wu Cun.) Brother Wanqiu is not in the co-op—this is because there is old text to copy; so I specifically copied it—Zhi Er) can now be regarded as hating me). "Look": When talking about me agreeing to "help with the friendship of friends," he called me "brother," but when talking about not helping him later, he spoke harshly, calling me "dog" and "Zhi Yu's flow." In this way, isn't Mr. Wu Cun's "righteousness" clear enough?

However, this also has a lineage. For example, if he wants to be Dian Wei, the gatekeeper for the master, he will not hesitate to praise me as Liao Hua, the "vanguard," and when he feels "enough suffering" after being skinned like a dog, he will scold me as a "scoundrel." He feels that "scoundrel" is still the opponent of "dog," so in order to confuse people's eyes and ears, he takes the preemptive measure of calling people "dogs." Like Mr. Wu Cun, he can only learn the "old methods." There is no "brilliant" method.

"If ×× doesn't agree, I hope he runs a director's school so I can worship him as an old man."

What is an "old man"? Only "the likes of Wu Cun" fully understand this. As for the "director school," it seems that "the theatrical predecessor Xiang Peiliang has already said that if you want to 'rebel' and 'roar,' please show your achievements on the stage.

(Confucius said: They are jackals of the same hill, why give many examples.)

The 11-volume Cantonese film "Daiyu Burying Flowers" is coming to Shanghai. Readers, what are your thoughts?

(Confucius said: I remember Mr. Zhang Shichuan's "Mrs. Mai.")

Lion's Roar 185

The Lion's Roar Drama Society of this city, which has been clamoring for a long time, has decided to hold its first public performance at the Jincheng Grand Theater starting on the 30th of this month. The plays are Tian Han's "Death of a Famous Actor" and the famous play by the playwright Ibsen "Ghosts." The actors are all famous veterans of Northern and Southern drama working together. The wonderfulness of the performance is expected. Tickets are now on sale, and seat reservations are very enthusiastic every day. It is expected that it will be crowded during the performance. Those who want good seats should buy tickets early.

Bright Moon Will Hold a Large-Scale Public Performance 186

Famous Movie Stars and Singers Participate

The Bright Moon Song and Dance Troupe, the birthplace of Chinese song and dance talents, has been established for fifteen years. To commemorate the occasion, a grand celebration will be launched, led by Li Jinhui, inviting famous movie stars and singers to perform. Participants include Li Minghui, Li Lili, Bai Hong, Li Mingjian, Zhou Xuan, Yan Fei, Yan Hua, etc. The programs arranged are wonderful and novel, and have never been seen before. The most magnificent and richest of them is the play "Peach Blossom Prince," which is enough to create a new record for the song and dance world. Li Minghui and Li Lili have not appeared on the stage for a long time. This decision to take the stage is a rare opportunity. It is heard that the performance location is at the Jincheng Grand Theater, and the date is set for the beginning of next month. It is expected that it will cause a sensation throughout Shanghai at that time.

Ox Nose Second Collection Published 187

China's humorous comic clown "Ox Nose" is scattered in major graphic magazines in the North and South. Since the publication of the first collection, it has been popular throughout the country. The second collection is even better, with more sophisticated techniques, more refined lines, and more profound themes, making people never tire of watching it. The little Ox Nose is even more exciting, deeply containing serious training, but depicted with light lines, interspersed with four pages of large-scale grand scenes "Ox Nose's Grand Funeral," exquisitely crafted, with a variety of shapes and colors, full of fun. The back cover is even more valuable, with "Vegetable Ox Nose" and "God of Wealth Face" made of silver coins, which is extremely ingenious. The ordinary edition is only sold for fifteen cents, breaking all medical reports' low prices. It has been published on the 26th of this month and is exclusively sold by the China Book Company.
